   39 import static java.lang.constant.ConstantDescs.BSM_EXPLICIT_CAST;
   40 import static java.lang.constant.ConstantDescs.CD_char;
   41 import static java.lang.constant.ConstantDescs.CD_int;
   42 import static java.lang.constant.ConstantDescs.DEFAULT_NAME;

   44 /**
   45  * The {@code Character} class wraps a value of the primitive
   46  * type {@code char} in an object. An object of class
   47  * {@code Character} contains a single field whose type is
   48  * {@code char}.
   49  * <p>
   50  * In addition, this class provides a large number of static methods for
   51  * determining a character's category (lowercase letter, digit, etc.)
   52  * and for converting characters from uppercase to lowercase and vice
   53  * versa.
   54  *
   55  * <h2><a id="conformance">Unicode Conformance</a></h2>
   56  * <p>
   57  * The fields and methods of class {@code Character} are defined in terms
   58  * of character information from the Unicode Standard, specifically the
   59  * <i>UnicodeData</i> file that is part of the Unicode Character Database.
   60  * This file specifies properties including name and category for every
   61  * assigned Unicode code point or character range. The file is available
   62  * from the Unicode Consortium at
   63  * <a href="http://www.unicode.org">http://www.unicode.org</a>.
   64  * <p>
   65  * Character information is based on the Unicode Standard, version 13.0.
   66  *
   67  * <h2><a id="unicode">Unicode Character Representations</a></h2>
   68  *
   69  * <p>The {@code char} data type (and therefore the value that a
   70  * {@code Character} object encapsulates) are based on the
   71  * original Unicode specification, which defined characters as
   72  * fixed-width 16-bit entities. The Unicode Standard has since been
   73  * changed to allow for characters whose representation requires more
   74  * than 16 bits.  The range of legal <em>code point</em>s is now
   75  * U+0000 to U+10FFFF, known as <em>Unicode scalar value</em>.
   76  * (Refer to the <a
   77  * href="http://www.unicode.org/reports/tr27/#notation"><i>
   78  * definition</i></a> of the U+<i>n</i> notation in the Unicode
   79  * Standard.)
   80  *
   81  * <p><a id="BMP">The set of characters from U+0000 to U+FFFF</a> is
   82  * sometimes referred to as the <em>Basic Multilingual Plane (BMP)</em>.
   83  * <a id="supplementary">Characters</a> whose code points are greater
   84  * than U+FFFF are called <em>supplementary character</em>s.  The Java
   85  * platform uses the UTF-16 representation in {@code char} arrays and
   86  * in the {@code String} and {@code StringBuffer} classes. In
   87  * this representation, supplementary characters are represented as a pair
   88  * of {@code char} values, the first from the <em>high-surrogates</em>
   89  * range, (&#92;uD800-&#92;uDBFF), the second from the
   90  * <em>low-surrogates</em> range (&#92;uDC00-&#92;uDFFF).
   91  *
   92  * <p>A {@code char} value, therefore, represents Basic
   93  * Multilingual Plane (BMP) code points, including the surrogate
   94  * code points, or code units of the UTF-16 encoding. An
   95  * {@code int} value represents all Unicode code points,
   96  * including supplementary code points. The lower (least significant)
   97  * 21 bits of {@code int} are used to represent Unicode code
   98  * points and the upper (most significant) 11 bits must be zero.
   99  * Unless otherwise specified, the behavior with respect to
  100  * supplementary characters and surrogate {@code char} values is
  101  * as follows:
  102  *
  103  * <ul>
  104  * <li>The methods that only accept a {@code char} value cannot support
  105  * supplementary characters. They treat {@code char} values from the
  106  * surrogate ranges as undefined characters. For example,
  107  * {@code Character.isLetter('\u005CuD840')} returns {@code false}, even though
  108  * this specific value if followed by any low-surrogate value in a string
  109  * would represent a letter.
  110  *
  111  * <li>The methods that accept an {@code int} value support all
  112  * Unicode characters, including supplementary characters. For
  113  * example, {@code Character.isLetter(0x2F81A)} returns
  114  * {@code true} because the code point value represents a letter
  115  * (a CJK ideograph).
  116  * </ul>
  117  *
  118  * <p>In the Java SE API documentation, <em>Unicode code point</em> is
  119  * used for character values in the range between U+0000 and U+10FFFF,
  120  * and <em>Unicode code unit</em> is used for 16-bit
  121  * {@code char} values that are code units of the <em>UTF-16</em>
  122  * encoding. For more information on Unicode terminology, refer to the
  123  * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/">Unicode Glossary</a>.
  124  *
  125  * @author  Lee Boynton
  126  * @author  Guy Steele
  127  * @author  Akira Tanaka
  128  * @author  Martin Buchholz
  129  * @author  Ulf Zibis
  130  * @since   1.0
  131  */
  132 public final
  133 class Character implements java.io.Serializable, Comparable<Character>, Constable {
  134     /**
  135      * The minimum radix available for conversion to and from strings.
  136      * The constant value of this field is the smallest value permitted
  137      * for the radix argument in radix-conversion methods such as the
  138      * {@code digit} method, the {@code forDigit} method, and the
  139      * {@code toString} method of class {@code Integer}.
  140      *
  141      * @see     Character#digit(char, int)
  142      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
  143      * @see     Integer#toString(int, int)
  144      * @see     Integer#valueOf(String)
  145      */
  146     public static final int MIN_RADIX = 2;
  147 
  148     /**
  149      * The maximum radix available for conversion to and from strings.
  150      * The constant value of this field is the largest value permitted
  151      * for the radix argument in radix-conversion methods such as the
  152      * {@code digit} method, the {@code forDigit} method, and the
  153      * {@code toString} method of class {@code Integer}.
  154      *
  155      * @see     Character#digit(char, int)
  156      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
  157      * @see     Integer#toString(int, int)
  158      * @see     Integer#valueOf(String)
  159      */
  160     public static final int MAX_RADIX = 36;
  161 
  162     /**
  163      * The constant value of this field is the smallest value of type
  164      * {@code char}, {@code '\u005Cu0000'}.
  165      *
  166      * @since   1.0.2
  167      */
  168     public static final char MIN_VALUE = '\u0000';
  169 
  170     /**
  171      * The constant value of this field is the largest value of type
  172      * {@code char}, {@code '\u005CuFFFF'}.
  173      *
  174      * @since   1.0.2
  175      */
  176     public static final char MAX_VALUE = '\uFFFF';

  612 
  613     /**
  614      * Returns an {@link Optional} containing the nominal descriptor for this
  615      * instance.
  616      *
  617      * @return an {@link Optional} describing the {@linkplain Character} instance
  618      * @since 15
  619      */
  620     @Override
  621     public Optional<DynamicConstantDesc<Character>> describeConstable() {
  622         return Optional.of(DynamicConstantDesc.ofNamed(BSM_EXPLICIT_CAST, DEFAULT_NAME, CD_char, (int) value));
  623     }
  624 
  625     /**
  626      * Instances of this class represent particular subsets of the Unicode
  627      * character set.  The only family of subsets defined in the
  628      * {@code Character} class is {@link Character.UnicodeBlock}.
  629      * Other portions of the Java API may define other subsets for their
  630      * own purposes.
  631      *
  632      * @since 1.2
  633      */
  634     public static class Subset  {
  635 
  636         private String name;
  637 
  638         /**
  639          * Constructs a new {@code Subset} instance.
  640          *
  641          * @param  name  The name of this subset
  642          * @throws NullPointerException if name is {@code null}
  643          */
  644         protected Subset(String name) {
  645             if (name == null) {
  646                 throw new NullPointerException("name");
  647             }
  648             this.name = name;
  649         }
  650 
  651         /**
  652          * Compares two {@code Subset} objects for equality.
  653          * This method returns {@code true} if and only if
  654          * {@code this} and the argument refer to the same
  655          * object; since this method is {@code final}, this
  656          * guarantee holds for all subclasses.
  657          */
  658         public final boolean equals(Object obj) {
  659             return (this == obj);
  660         }
  661 
  662         /**
  663          * Returns the standard hash code as defined by the
  664          * {@link Object#hashCode} method.  This method
  665          * is {@code final} in order to ensure that the
  666          * {@code equals} and {@code hashCode} methods will
  667          * be consistent in all subclasses.
  668          */
  669         public final int hashCode() {
  670             return super.hashCode();
  671         }
  672 
  673         /**
  674          * Returns the name of this subset.
  675          */
  676         public final String toString() {
  677             return name;
  678         }
  679     }
  680 
  681     // See http://www.unicode.org/Public/UNIDATA/Blocks.txt
  682     // for the latest specification of Unicode Blocks.
  683 
  684     /**
  685      * A family of character subsets representing the character blocks in the
  686      * Unicode specification. Character blocks generally define characters
  687      * used for a specific script or purpose. A character is contained by
  688      * at most one Unicode block.
  689      *
  690      * @since 1.2
  691      */
  692     public static final class UnicodeBlock extends Subset {
  693         /**
  694          * 684 - the expected number of entities
  695          * 0.75 - the default load factor of HashMap
  696          */
  697         private static final int NUM_ENTITIES = 684;
  698         private static Map<String, UnicodeBlock> map =
  699                 new HashMap<>((int)(NUM_ENTITIES / 0.75f + 1.0f));
  700 
  701         /**
  702          * Creates a UnicodeBlock with the given identifier name.
  703          * This name must be the same as the block identifier.
  704          */
  705         private UnicodeBlock(String idName) {
  706             super(idName);
  707             map.put(idName, this);
  708         }
  709 
  710         /**
  711          * Creates a UnicodeBlock with the given identifier name and
  712          * alias name.
  713          */
  714         private UnicodeBlock(String idName, String alias) {
  715             this(idName);
  716             map.put(alias, this);
  717         }
  718 
  719         /**
  720          * Creates a UnicodeBlock with the given identifier name and
  721          * alias names.
  722          */
  723         private UnicodeBlock(String idName, String... aliases) {
  724             this(idName);
  725             for (String alias : aliases)
  726                 map.put(alias, this);
  727         }
  728

 4114         /**
 4115          * Returns the object representing the Unicode block containing the
 4116          * given character, or {@code null} if the character is not a
 4117          * member of a defined block.
 4118          *
 4119          * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle
 4120          * <a href="Character.html#supplementary"> supplementary
 4121          * characters</a>.  To support all Unicode characters, including
 4122          * supplementary characters, use the {@link #of(int)} method.
 4123          *
 4124          * @param   c  The character in question
 4125          * @return  The {@code UnicodeBlock} instance representing the
 4126          *          Unicode block of which this character is a member, or
 4127          *          {@code null} if the character is not a member of any
 4128          *          Unicode block
 4129          */
 4130         public static UnicodeBlock of(char c) {
 4131             return of((int)c);
 4132         }
 4133 
 4134         /**
 4135          * Returns the object representing the Unicode block
 4136          * containing the given character (Unicode code point), or
 4137          * {@code null} if the character is not a member of a
 4138          * defined block.
 4139          *
 4140          * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) in question.
 4141          * @return  The {@code UnicodeBlock} instance representing the
 4142          *          Unicode block of which this character is a member, or
 4143          *          {@code null} if the character is not a member of any
 4144          *          Unicode block
 4145          * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 4146          * {@code codePoint} is an invalid Unicode code point.
 4147          * @see Character#isValidCodePoint(int)
 4148          * @since   1.5
 4149          */
 4150         public static UnicodeBlock of(int codePoint) {
 4151             if (!isValidCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 4152                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(
 4153                     String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
 4154             }
 4155 
 4156             int top, bottom, current;
 4157             bottom = 0;
 4158             top = blockStarts.length;
 4159             current = top/2;
 4160 
 4161             // invariant: top > current >= bottom && codePoint >= unicodeBlockStarts[bottom]
 4162             while (top - bottom > 1) {
 4163                 if (codePoint >= blockStarts[current]) {
 4164                     bottom = current;
 4165                 } else {
 4166                     top = current;
 4167                 }
 4168                 current = (top + bottom) / 2;
 4169             }
 4170             return blocks[current];
 4171         }
 4172 
 4173         /**
 4174          * Returns the UnicodeBlock with the given name. Block
 4175          * names are determined by The Unicode Standard. The file
 4176          * {@code Blocks-<version>.txt} defines blocks for a particular
 4177          * version of the standard. The {@link Character} class specifies
 4178          * the version of the standard that it supports.
 4179          * <p>
 4180          * This method accepts block names in the following forms:
 4181          * <ol>
 4182          * <li> Canonical block names as defined by the Unicode Standard.
 4183          * For example, the standard defines a "Basic Latin" block. Therefore, this
 4184          * method accepts "Basic Latin" as a valid block name. The documentation of
 4185          * each UnicodeBlock provides the canonical name.
 4186          * <li>Canonical block names with all spaces removed. For example, "BasicLatin"
 4187          * is a valid block name for the "Basic Latin" block.
 4188          * <li>The text representation of each constant UnicodeBlock identifier.
 4189          * For example, this method will return the {@link #BASIC_LATIN} block if
 4190          * provided with the "BASIC_LATIN" name. This form replaces all spaces and
 4191          * hyphens in the canonical name with underscores.
 4192          * </ol>
 4193          * Finally, character case is ignored for all of the valid block name forms.
 4194          * For example, "BASIC_LATIN" and "basic_latin" are both valid block names.
 4195          * The en_US locale's case mapping rules are used to provide case-insensitive
 4196          * string comparisons for block name validation.
 4197          * <p>
 4198          * If the Unicode Standard changes block names, both the previous and
 4199          * current names will be accepted.
 4200          *
 4201          * @param blockName A {@code UnicodeBlock} name.
 4202          * @return The {@code UnicodeBlock} instance identified
 4203          *         by {@code blockName}
 4204          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code blockName} is an
 4205          *         invalid name
 4206          * @throws NullPointerException if {@code blockName} is null
 4207          * @since 1.5
 4208          */
 4209         public static final UnicodeBlock forName(String blockName) {
 4210             UnicodeBlock block = map.get(blockName.toUpperCase(Locale.US));
 4211             if (block == null) {
 4212                 throw new IllegalArgumentException("Not a valid block name: "
 4213                             + blockName);
 4214             }
 4215             return block;
 4216         }
 4217     }

 8423 
 8424         /**
 8425          * Returns the enum constant representing the Unicode script of which
 8426          * the given character (Unicode code point) is assigned to.
 8427          *
 8428          * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) in question.
 8429          * @return  The {@code UnicodeScript} constant representing the
 8430          *          Unicode script of which this character is assigned to.
 8431          *
 8432          * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 8433          * {@code codePoint} is an invalid Unicode code point.
 8434          * @see Character#isValidCodePoint(int)
 8435          *
 8436          */
 8437         public static UnicodeScript of(int codePoint) {
 8438             if (!isValidCodePoint(codePoint))
 8439                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(
 8440                     String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
 8441             int type = getType(codePoint);
 8442             // leave SURROGATE and PRIVATE_USE for table lookup
 8443             if (type == UNASSIGNED)
 8444                 return UNKNOWN;
 8445             int index = Arrays.binarySearch(scriptStarts, codePoint);
 8446             if (index < 0)
 8447                 index = -index - 2;
 8448             return scripts[index];
 8449         }
 8450 
 8451         /**
 8452          * Returns the UnicodeScript constant with the given Unicode script
 8453          * name or the script name alias. Script names and their aliases are
 8454          * determined by The Unicode Standard. The files {@code Scripts<version>.txt}
 8455          * and {@code PropertyValueAliases<version>.txt} define script names
 8456          * and the script name aliases for a particular version of the
 8457          * standard. The {@link Character} class specifies the version of
 8458          * the standard that it supports.
 8459          * <p>
 8460          * Character case is ignored for all of the valid script names.
 8461          * The en_US locale's case mapping rules are used to provide
 8462          * case-insensitive string comparisons for script name validation.
 8463          *
 8464          * @param scriptName A {@code UnicodeScript} name.
 8465          * @return The {@code UnicodeScript} constant identified
 8466          *         by {@code scriptName}
 8467          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code scriptName} is an
 8468          *         invalid name
 8469          * @throws NullPointerException if {@code scriptName} is null
 8470          */
 8471         public static final UnicodeScript forName(String scriptName) {
 8472             scriptName = scriptName.toUpperCase(Locale.ENGLISH);
 8473                                  //.replace(' ', '_'));
 8474             UnicodeScript sc = aliases.get(scriptName);
 8475             if (sc != null)
 8476                 return sc;
 8477             return valueOf(scriptName);
 8478         }
 8479     }
 8480 
 8481     /**
 8482      * The value of the {@code Character}.
 8483      *
 8484      * @serial
 8485      */
 8486     private final char value;
 8487 
 8488     /** use serialVersionUID from JDK 1.0.2 for interoperability */
 8489     @java.io.Serial
 8490     private static final long serialVersionUID = 3786198910865385080L;
 8491 
 8492     /**
 8493      * Constructs a newly allocated {@code Character} object that
 8494      * represents the specified {@code char} value.
 8495      *
 8496      * @param  value   the value to be represented by the
 8497      *                  {@code Character} object.
 8498      *
 8499      * @deprecated
 8500      * It is rarely appropriate to use this constructor. The static factory
 8501      * {@link #valueOf(char)} is generally a better choice, as it is
 8502      * likely to yield significantly better space and time performance.
 8503      */
 8504     @Deprecated(since="9")
 8505     public Character(char value) {
 8506         this.value = value;
 8507     }
 8508 
 8509     private static class CharacterCache {
 8510         private CharacterCache(){}
 8511 
 8512         static final Character[] cache;
 8513         static Character[] archivedCache;
 8514 
 8515         static {
 8516             int size = 127 + 1;
 8517 
 8518             // Load and use the archived cache if it exists
 8519             VM.initializeFromArchive(CharacterCache.class);
 8520             if (archivedCache == null || archivedCache.length != size) {
 8521                 Character[] c = new Character[size];
 8522                 for (int i = 0; i < size; i++) {
 8523                     c[i] = new Character((char) i);
 8524                 }
 8525                 archivedCache = c;
 8526             }
 8527             cache = archivedCache;
 8528         }
 8529     }
 8530 
 8531     /**
 8532      * Returns a {@code Character} instance representing the specified
 8533      * {@code char} value.
 8534      * If a new {@code Character} instance is not required, this method
 8535      * should generally be used in preference to the constructor
 8536      * {@link #Character(char)}, as this method is likely to yield
 8537      * significantly better space and time performance by caching
 8538      * frequently requested values.
 8539      *
 8540      * This method will always cache values in the range {@code
 8541      * '\u005Cu0000'} to {@code '\u005Cu007F'}, inclusive, and may
 8542      * cache other values outside of this range.
 8543      *
 8544      * @param  c a char value.
 8545      * @return a {@code Character} instance representing {@code c}.
 8546      * @since  1.5
 8547      */
 8548     @HotSpotIntrinsicCandidate
 8549     public static Character valueOf(char c) {
 8550         if (c <= 127) { // must cache
 8551             return CharacterCache.cache[(int)c];
 8552         }
 8553         return new Character(c);
 8554     }
 8555 
 8556     /**
 8557      * Returns the value of this {@code Character} object.
 8558      * @return  the primitive {@code char} value represented by
 8559      *          this object.
 8560      */
 8561     @HotSpotIntrinsicCandidate
 8562     public char charValue() {
 8563         return value;
 8564     }
 8565 
 8566     /**
 8567      * Returns a hash code for this {@code Character}; equal to the result
 8568      * of invoking {@code charValue()}.
 8569      *
 8570      * @return a hash code value for this {@code Character}
 8571      */
 8572     @Override
 8573     public int hashCode() {
 8574         return Character.hashCode(value);
 8575     }
 8576 
 8577     /**
 8578      * Returns a hash code for a {@code char} value; compatible with
 8579      * {@code Character.hashCode()}.
 8580      *
 8581      * @since 1.8
 8582      *
 8583      * @param value The {@code char} for which to return a hash code.
 8584      * @return a hash code value for a {@code char} value.
 8585      */
 8586     public static int hashCode(char value) {
 8587         return (int)value;
 8588     }
 8589 
 8590     /**
 8591      * Compares this object against the specified object.
 8592      * The result is {@code true} if and only if the argument is not
 8593      * {@code null} and is a {@code Character} object that
 8594      * represents the same {@code char} value as this object.
 8595      *
 8596      * @param   obj   the object to compare with.
 8597      * @return  {@code true} if the objects are the same;
 8598      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 8599      */
 8600     public boolean equals(Object obj) {
 8601         if (obj instanceof Character) {
 8602             return value == ((Character)obj).charValue();
 8603         }
 8604         return false;
 8605     }
 8606 
 8607     /**
 8608      * Returns a {@code String} object representing this
 8609      * {@code Character}'s value.  The result is a string of
 8610      * length 1 whose sole component is the primitive
 8611      * {@code char} value represented by this
 8612      * {@code Character} object.
 8613      *
 8614      * @return  a string representation of this object.
 8615      */
 8616     public String toString() {
 8617         return String.valueOf(value);
 8618     }
 8619 
 8620     /**
 8621      * Returns a {@code String} object representing the
 8622      * specified {@code char}.  The result is a string of length
 8623      * 1 consisting solely of the specified {@code char}.
 8624      *
 8625      * @apiNote This method cannot handle <a
 8626      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 8627      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 8628      * the {@link #toString(int)} method.
 8629      *
 8630      * @param c the {@code char} to be converted
 8631      * @return the string representation of the specified {@code char}
 8632      * @since 1.4
 8633      */
 8634     public static String toString(char c) {
 8635         return String.valueOf(c);
 8636     }
 8637 
 8638     /**
 8639      * Returns a {@code String} object representing the
 8640      * specified character (Unicode code point).  The result is a string of
 8641      * length 1 or 2, consisting solely of the specified {@code codePoint}.
 8642      *
 8643      * @param codePoint the {@code codePoint} to be converted
 8644      * @return the string representation of the specified {@code codePoint}
 8645      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 8646      *      {@code codePoint} is not a {@linkplain #isValidCodePoint
 8647      *      valid Unicode code point}.
 8648      * @since 11
 8649      */
 8650     public static String toString(int codePoint) {
 8651         return String.valueOfCodePoint(codePoint);
 8652     }
 8653 
 8654     /**
 8655      * Determines whether the specified code point is a valid
 8656      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#code_point">
 8657      * Unicode code point value</a>.
 8658      *
 8659      * @param  codePoint the Unicode code point to be tested
 8660      * @return {@code true} if the specified code point value is between
 8661      *         {@link #MIN_CODE_POINT} and
 8662      *         {@link #MAX_CODE_POINT} inclusive;
 8663      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8664      * @since  1.5
 8665      */
 8666     public static boolean isValidCodePoint(int codePoint) {
 8667         // Optimized form of:
 8668         //     codePoint >= MIN_CODE_POINT && codePoint <= MAX_CODE_POINT
 8669         int plane = codePoint >>> 16;
 8670         return plane < ((MAX_CODE_POINT + 1) >>> 16);
 8671     }
 8672 
 8673     /**
 8674      * Determines whether the specified character (Unicode code point)
 8675      * is in the <a href="#BMP">Basic Multilingual Plane (BMP)</a>.
 8676      * Such code points can be represented using a single {@code char}.
 8677      *
 8678      * @param  codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested
 8679      * @return {@code true} if the specified code point is between
 8680      *         {@link #MIN_VALUE} and {@link #MAX_VALUE} inclusive;
 8681      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8682      * @since  1.7
 8683      */
 8684     public static boolean isBmpCodePoint(int codePoint) {
 8685         return codePoint >>> 16 == 0;
 8686         // Optimized form of:
 8687         //     codePoint >= MIN_VALUE && codePoint <= MAX_VALUE
 8688         // We consistently use logical shift (>>>) to facilitate
 8689         // additional runtime optimizations.
 8690     }
 8691 
 8692     /**
 8693      * Determines whether the specified character (Unicode code point)
 8694      * is in the <a href="#supplementary">supplementary character</a> range.
 8695      *
 8696      * @param  codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested
 8697      * @return {@code true} if the specified code point is between
 8698      *         {@link #MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT} and
 8699      *         {@link #MAX_CODE_POINT} inclusive;
 8700      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8701      * @since  1.5
 8702      */
 8703     public static boolean isSupplementaryCodePoint(int codePoint) {
 8704         return codePoint >= MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT
 8705             && codePoint <  MAX_CODE_POINT + 1;
 8706     }
 8707 
 8708     /**
 8709      * Determines if the given {@code char} value is a
 8710      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#high_surrogate_code_unit">
 8711      * Unicode high-surrogate code unit</a>
 8712      * (also known as <i>leading-surrogate code unit</i>).
 8713      *
 8714      * <p>Such values do not represent characters by themselves,
 8715      * but are used in the representation of
 8716      * <a href="#supplementary">supplementary characters</a>
 8717      * in the UTF-16 encoding.
 8718      *
 8719      * @param  ch the {@code char} value to be tested.
 8720      * @return {@code true} if the {@code char} value is between
 8721      *         {@link #MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE} and
 8722      *         {@link #MAX_HIGH_SURROGATE} inclusive;
 8723      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8724      * @see    Character#isLowSurrogate(char)
 8725      * @see    Character.UnicodeBlock#of(int)
 8726      * @since  1.5
 8727      */
 8728     public static boolean isHighSurrogate(char ch) {
 8729         // Help VM constant-fold; MAX_HIGH_SURROGATE + 1 == MIN_LOW_SURROGATE
 8730         return ch >= MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE && ch < (MAX_HIGH_SURROGATE + 1);
 8731     }
 8732 
 8733     /**
 8734      * Determines if the given {@code char} value is a
 8735      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#low_surrogate_code_unit">
 8736      * Unicode low-surrogate code unit</a>
 8737      * (also known as <i>trailing-surrogate code unit</i>).
 8738      *
 8739      * <p>Such values do not represent characters by themselves,
 8740      * but are used in the representation of
 8741      * <a href="#supplementary">supplementary characters</a>
 8742      * in the UTF-16 encoding.
 8743      *
 8744      * @param  ch the {@code char} value to be tested.
 8745      * @return {@code true} if the {@code char} value is between
 8746      *         {@link #MIN_LOW_SURROGATE} and
 8747      *         {@link #MAX_LOW_SURROGATE} inclusive;
 8748      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8749      * @see    Character#isHighSurrogate(char)
 8750      * @since  1.5
 8751      */
 8752     public static boolean isLowSurrogate(char ch) {
 8753         return ch >= MIN_LOW_SURROGATE && ch < (MAX_LOW_SURROGATE + 1);
 8754     }
 8755 
 8756     /**
 8757      * Determines if the given {@code char} value is a Unicode
 8758      * <i>surrogate code unit</i>.
 8759      *
 8760      * <p>Such values do not represent characters by themselves,
 8761      * but are used in the representation of
 8762      * <a href="#supplementary">supplementary characters</a>
 8763      * in the UTF-16 encoding.
 8764      *
 8765      * <p>A char value is a surrogate code unit if and only if it is either
 8766      * a {@linkplain #isLowSurrogate(char) low-surrogate code unit} or
 8767      * a {@linkplain #isHighSurrogate(char) high-surrogate code unit}.
 8768      *
 8769      * @param  ch the {@code char} value to be tested.
 8770      * @return {@code true} if the {@code char} value is between
 8771      *         {@link #MIN_SURROGATE} and
 8772      *         {@link #MAX_SURROGATE} inclusive;
 8773      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8774      * @since  1.7
 8775      */
 8776     public static boolean isSurrogate(char ch) {
 8777         return ch >= MIN_SURROGATE && ch < (MAX_SURROGATE + 1);
 8778     }
 8779 
 8780     /**
 8781      * Determines whether the specified pair of {@code char}
 8782      * values is a valid
 8783      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_pair">
 8784      * Unicode surrogate pair</a>.
 8785      *
 8786      * <p>This method is equivalent to the expression:
 8787      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
 8788      * isHighSurrogate(high) && isLowSurrogate(low)
 8789      * }</pre></blockquote>
 8790      *
 8791      * @param  high the high-surrogate code value to be tested
 8792      * @param  low the low-surrogate code value to be tested
 8793      * @return {@code true} if the specified high and
 8794      * low-surrogate code values represent a valid surrogate pair;
 8795      * {@code false} otherwise.
 8796      * @since  1.5
 8797      */
 8798     public static boolean isSurrogatePair(char high, char low) {
 8799         return isHighSurrogate(high) && isLowSurrogate(low);
 8800     }
 8801 
 8802     /**
 8803      * Determines the number of {@code char} values needed to
 8804      * represent the specified character (Unicode code point). If the
 8805      * specified character is equal to or greater than 0x10000, then
 8806      * the method returns 2. Otherwise, the method returns 1.
 8807      *
 8808      * <p>This method doesn't validate the specified character to be a
 8809      * valid Unicode code point. The caller must validate the
 8810      * character value using {@link #isValidCodePoint(int) isValidCodePoint}
 8811      * if necessary.
 8812      *
 8813      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 8814      * @return  2 if the character is a valid supplementary character; 1 otherwise.
 8815      * @see     Character#isSupplementaryCodePoint(int)
 8816      * @since   1.5
 8817      */
 8818     public static int charCount(int codePoint) {
 8819         return codePoint >= MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT ? 2 : 1;
 8820     }
 8821 
 8822     /**
 8823      * Converts the specified surrogate pair to its supplementary code
 8824      * point value. This method does not validate the specified
 8825      * surrogate pair. The caller must validate it using {@link
 8826      * #isSurrogatePair(char, char) isSurrogatePair} if necessary.
 8827      *
 8828      * @param  high the high-surrogate code unit
 8829      * @param  low the low-surrogate code unit
 8830      * @return the supplementary code point composed from the
 8831      *         specified surrogate pair.
 8832      * @since  1.5
 8833      */
 8834     public static int toCodePoint(char high, char low) {
 8835         // Optimized form of:
 8836         // return ((high - MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE) << 10)
 8837         //         + (low - MIN_LOW_SURROGATE)
 8838         //         + MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT;
 8839         return ((high << 10) + low) + (MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT
 8840                                        - (MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE << 10)
 8841                                        - MIN_LOW_SURROGATE);
 8842     }
 8843 
 8844     /**
 8845      * Returns the code point at the given index of the
 8846      * {@code CharSequence}. If the {@code char} value at
 8847      * the given index in the {@code CharSequence} is in the
 8848      * high-surrogate range, the following index is less than the
 8849      * length of the {@code CharSequence}, and the
 8850      * {@code char} value at the following index is in the
 8851      * low-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8852      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8853      * the {@code char} value at the given index is returned.
 8854      *
 8855      * @param seq a sequence of {@code char} values (Unicode code
 8856      * units)
 8857      * @param index the index to the {@code char} values (Unicode
 8858      * code units) in {@code seq} to be converted
 8859      * @return the Unicode code point at the given index
 8860      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code seq} is null.
 8861      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the value
 8862      * {@code index} is negative or not less than
 8863      * {@link CharSequence#length() seq.length()}.
 8864      * @since  1.5
 8865      */
 8866     public static int codePointAt(CharSequence seq, int index) {
 8867         char c1 = seq.charAt(index);
 8868         if (isHighSurrogate(c1) && ++index < seq.length()) {
 8869             char c2 = seq.charAt(index);
 8870             if (isLowSurrogate(c2)) {
 8871                 return toCodePoint(c1, c2);
 8872             }
 8873         }
 8874         return c1;
 8875     }
 8876 
 8877     /**
 8878      * Returns the code point at the given index of the
 8879      * {@code char} array. If the {@code char} value at
 8880      * the given index in the {@code char} array is in the
 8881      * high-surrogate range, the following index is less than the
 8882      * length of the {@code char} array, and the
 8883      * {@code char} value at the following index is in the
 8884      * low-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8885      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8886      * the {@code char} value at the given index is returned.
 8887      *
 8888      * @param a the {@code char} array
 8889      * @param index the index to the {@code char} values (Unicode
 8890      * code units) in the {@code char} array to be converted
 8891      * @return the Unicode code point at the given index
 8892      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 8893      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the value
 8894      * {@code index} is negative or not less than
 8895      * the length of the {@code char} array.
 8896      * @since  1.5
 8897      */
 8898     public static int codePointAt(char[] a, int index) {
 8899         return codePointAtImpl(a, index, a.length);
 8900     }
 8901 
 8902     /**
 8903      * Returns the code point at the given index of the
 8904      * {@code char} array, where only array elements with
 8905      * {@code index} less than {@code limit} can be used. If
 8906      * the {@code char} value at the given index in the
 8907      * {@code char} array is in the high-surrogate range, the
 8908      * following index is less than the {@code limit}, and the
 8909      * {@code char} value at the following index is in the
 8910      * low-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8911      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8912      * the {@code char} value at the given index is returned.
 8913      *
 8914      * @param a the {@code char} array
 8915      * @param index the index to the {@code char} values (Unicode
 8916      * code units) in the {@code char} array to be converted
 8917      * @param limit the index after the last array element that
 8918      * can be used in the {@code char} array
 8919      * @return the Unicode code point at the given index
 8920      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 8921      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the {@code index}
 8922      * argument is negative or not less than the {@code limit}
 8923      * argument, or if the {@code limit} argument is negative or
 8924      * greater than the length of the {@code char} array.
 8925      * @since  1.5
 8926      */
 8927     public static int codePointAt(char[] a, int index, int limit) {
 8928         if (index >= limit || limit < 0 || limit > a.length) {
 8929             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 8930         }
 8931         return codePointAtImpl(a, index, limit);
 8932     }
 8933 
 8934     // throws ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException if index out of bounds
 8935     static int codePointAtImpl(char[] a, int index, int limit) {
 8936         char c1 = a[index];
 8937         if (isHighSurrogate(c1) && ++index < limit) {
 8938             char c2 = a[index];
 8939             if (isLowSurrogate(c2)) {
 8940                 return toCodePoint(c1, c2);
 8941             }
 8942         }
 8943         return c1;
 8944     }
 8945 
 8946     /**
 8947      * Returns the code point preceding the given index of the
 8948      * {@code CharSequence}. If the {@code char} value at
 8949      * {@code (index - 1)} in the {@code CharSequence} is in
 8950      * the low-surrogate range, {@code (index - 2)} is not
 8951      * negative, and the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 2)}
 8952      * in the {@code CharSequence} is in the
 8953      * high-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8954      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8955      * the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 1)} is
 8956      * returned.
 8957      *
 8958      * @param seq the {@code CharSequence} instance
 8959      * @param index the index following the code point that should be returned
 8960      * @return the Unicode code point value before the given index.
 8961      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code seq} is null.
 8962      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the {@code index}
 8963      * argument is less than 1 or greater than {@link
 8964      * CharSequence#length() seq.length()}.
 8965      * @since  1.5
 8966      */
 8967     public static int codePointBefore(CharSequence seq, int index) {
 8968         char c2 = seq.charAt(--index);
 8969         if (isLowSurrogate(c2) && index > 0) {
 8970             char c1 = seq.charAt(--index);
 8971             if (isHighSurrogate(c1)) {
 8972                 return toCodePoint(c1, c2);
 8973             }
 8974         }
 8975         return c2;
 8976     }
 8977 
 8978     /**
 8979      * Returns the code point preceding the given index of the
 8980      * {@code char} array. If the {@code char} value at
 8981      * {@code (index - 1)} in the {@code char} array is in
 8982      * the low-surrogate range, {@code (index - 2)} is not
 8983      * negative, and the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 2)}
 8984      * in the {@code char} array is in the
 8985      * high-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8986      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8987      * the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 1)} is
 8988      * returned.
 8989      *
 8990      * @param a the {@code char} array
 8991      * @param index the index following the code point that should be returned
 8992      * @return the Unicode code point value before the given index.
 8993      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 8994      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the {@code index}
 8995      * argument is less than 1 or greater than the length of the
 8996      * {@code char} array
 8997      * @since  1.5
 8998      */
 8999     public static int codePointBefore(char[] a, int index) {
 9000         return codePointBeforeImpl(a, index, 0);
 9001     }
 9002 
 9003     /**
 9004      * Returns the code point preceding the given index of the
 9005      * {@code char} array, where only array elements with
 9006      * {@code index} greater than or equal to {@code start}
 9007      * can be used. If the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 1)}
 9008      * in the {@code char} array is in the
 9009      * low-surrogate range, {@code (index - 2)} is not less than
 9010      * {@code start}, and the {@code char} value at
 9011      * {@code (index - 2)} in the {@code char} array is in
 9012      * the high-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 9013      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 9014      * the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 1)} is
 9015      * returned.
 9016      *
 9017      * @param a the {@code char} array
 9018      * @param index the index following the code point that should be returned
 9019      * @param start the index of the first array element in the
 9020      * {@code char} array
 9021      * @return the Unicode code point value before the given index.
 9022      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 9023      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the {@code index}
 9024      * argument is not greater than the {@code start} argument or
 9025      * is greater than the length of the {@code char} array, or
 9026      * if the {@code start} argument is negative or not less than
 9027      * the length of the {@code char} array.
 9028      * @since  1.5
 9029      */
 9030     public static int codePointBefore(char[] a, int index, int start) {
 9031         if (index <= start || start < 0 || start >= a.length) {
 9032             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9033         }
 9034         return codePointBeforeImpl(a, index, start);
 9035     }
 9036 
 9037     // throws ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException if index-1 out of bounds
 9038     static int codePointBeforeImpl(char[] a, int index, int start) {
 9039         char c2 = a[--index];
 9040         if (isLowSurrogate(c2) && index > start) {
 9041             char c1 = a[--index];
 9042             if (isHighSurrogate(c1)) {
 9043                 return toCodePoint(c1, c2);
 9044             }
 9045         }
 9046         return c2;
 9047     }
 9048 
 9049     /**
 9050      * Returns the leading surrogate (a
 9051      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#high_surrogate_code_unit">
 9052      * high surrogate code unit</a>) of the
 9053      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_pair">
 9054      * surrogate pair</a>
 9055      * representing the specified supplementary character (Unicode
 9056      * code point) in the UTF-16 encoding.  If the specified character
 9057      * is not a
 9058      * <a href="Character.html#supplementary">supplementary character</a>,
 9059      * an unspecified {@code char} is returned.
 9060      *
 9061      * <p>If
 9062      * {@link #isSupplementaryCodePoint isSupplementaryCodePoint(x)}
 9063      * is {@code true}, then
 9064      * {@link #isHighSurrogate isHighSurrogate}{@code (highSurrogate(x))} and
 9065      * {@link #toCodePoint toCodePoint}{@code (highSurrogate(x), }{@link #lowSurrogate lowSurrogate}{@code (x)) == x}
 9066      * are also always {@code true}.
 9067      *
 9068      * @param   codePoint a supplementary character (Unicode code point)
 9069      * @return  the leading surrogate code unit used to represent the
 9070      *          character in the UTF-16 encoding
 9071      * @since   1.7
 9072      */
 9073     public static char highSurrogate(int codePoint) {
 9074         return (char) ((codePoint >>> 10)
 9075             + (MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE - (MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT >>> 10)));
 9076     }
 9077 
 9078     /**
 9079      * Returns the trailing surrogate (a
 9080      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#low_surrogate_code_unit">
 9081      * low surrogate code unit</a>) of the
 9082      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_pair">
 9083      * surrogate pair</a>
 9084      * representing the specified supplementary character (Unicode
 9085      * code point) in the UTF-16 encoding.  If the specified character
 9086      * is not a
 9087      * <a href="Character.html#supplementary">supplementary character</a>,
 9088      * an unspecified {@code char} is returned.
 9089      *
 9090      * <p>If
 9091      * {@link #isSupplementaryCodePoint isSupplementaryCodePoint(x)}
 9092      * is {@code true}, then
 9093      * {@link #isLowSurrogate isLowSurrogate}{@code (lowSurrogate(x))} and
 9094      * {@link #toCodePoint toCodePoint}{@code (}{@link #highSurrogate highSurrogate}{@code (x), lowSurrogate(x)) == x}
 9095      * are also always {@code true}.
 9096      *
 9097      * @param   codePoint a supplementary character (Unicode code point)
 9098      * @return  the trailing surrogate code unit used to represent the
 9099      *          character in the UTF-16 encoding
 9100      * @since   1.7
 9101      */
 9102     public static char lowSurrogate(int codePoint) {
 9103         return (char) ((codePoint & 0x3ff) + MIN_LOW_SURROGATE);
 9104     }
 9105 
 9106     /**
 9107      * Converts the specified character (Unicode code point) to its
 9108      * UTF-16 representation. If the specified code point is a BMP
 9109      * (Basic Multilingual Plane or Plane 0) value, the same value is
 9110      * stored in {@code dst[dstIndex]}, and 1 is returned. If the
 9111      * specified code point is a supplementary character, its
 9112      * surrogate values are stored in {@code dst[dstIndex]}
 9113      * (high-surrogate) and {@code dst[dstIndex+1]}
 9114      * (low-surrogate), and 2 is returned.
 9115      *
 9116      * @param  codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
 9117      * @param  dst an array of {@code char} in which the
 9118      * {@code codePoint}'s UTF-16 value is stored.
 9119      * @param dstIndex the start index into the {@code dst}
 9120      * array where the converted value is stored.
 9121      * @return 1 if the code point is a BMP code point, 2 if the
 9122      * code point is a supplementary code point.
 9123      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 9124      * {@code codePoint} is not a valid Unicode code point.
 9125      * @throws NullPointerException if the specified {@code dst} is null.
 9126      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if {@code dstIndex}
 9127      * is negative or not less than {@code dst.length}, or if
 9128      * {@code dst} at {@code dstIndex} doesn't have enough
 9129      * array element(s) to store the resulting {@code char}
 9130      * value(s). (If {@code dstIndex} is equal to
 9131      * {@code dst.length-1} and the specified
 9132      * {@code codePoint} is a supplementary character, the
 9133      * high-surrogate value is not stored in
 9134      * {@code dst[dstIndex]}.)
 9135      * @since  1.5
 9136      */
 9137     public static int toChars(int codePoint, char[] dst, int dstIndex) {
 9138         if (isBmpCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 9139             dst[dstIndex] = (char) codePoint;
 9140             return 1;
 9141         } else if (isValidCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 9142             toSurrogates(codePoint, dst, dstIndex);
 9143             return 2;
 9144         } else {
 9145             throw new IllegalArgumentException(
 9146                 String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
 9147         }
 9148     }
 9149 
 9150     /**
 9151      * Converts the specified character (Unicode code point) to its
 9152      * UTF-16 representation stored in a {@code char} array. If
 9153      * the specified code point is a BMP (Basic Multilingual Plane or
 9154      * Plane 0) value, the resulting {@code char} array has
 9155      * the same value as {@code codePoint}. If the specified code
 9156      * point is a supplementary code point, the resulting
 9157      * {@code char} array has the corresponding surrogate pair.
 9158      *
 9159      * @param  codePoint a Unicode code point
 9160      * @return a {@code char} array having
 9161      *         {@code codePoint}'s UTF-16 representation.
 9162      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 9163      * {@code codePoint} is not a valid Unicode code point.
 9164      * @since  1.5
 9165      */
 9166     public static char[] toChars(int codePoint) {
 9167         if (isBmpCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 9168             return new char[] { (char) codePoint };
 9169         } else if (isValidCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 9170             char[] result = new char[2];
 9171             toSurrogates(codePoint, result, 0);
 9172             return result;
 9173         } else {
 9174             throw new IllegalArgumentException(
 9175                 String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
 9176         }
 9177     }
 9178 
 9179     static void toSurrogates(int codePoint, char[] dst, int index) {
 9180         // We write elements "backwards" to guarantee all-or-nothing
 9181         dst[index+1] = lowSurrogate(codePoint);
 9182         dst[index] = highSurrogate(codePoint);
 9183     }
 9184 
 9185     /**
 9186      * Returns the number of Unicode code points in the text range of
 9187      * the specified char sequence. The text range begins at the
 9188      * specified {@code beginIndex} and extends to the
 9189      * {@code char} at index {@code endIndex - 1}. Thus the
 9190      * length (in {@code char}s) of the text range is
 9191      * {@code endIndex-beginIndex}. Unpaired surrogates within
 9192      * the text range count as one code point each.
 9193      *
 9194      * @param seq the char sequence
 9195      * @param beginIndex the index to the first {@code char} of
 9196      * the text range.
 9197      * @param endIndex the index after the last {@code char} of
 9198      * the text range.
 9199      * @return the number of Unicode code points in the specified text
 9200      * range
 9201      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code seq} is null.
 9202      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the
 9203      * {@code beginIndex} is negative, or {@code endIndex}
 9204      * is larger than the length of the given sequence, or
 9205      * {@code beginIndex} is larger than {@code endIndex}.
 9206      * @since  1.5
 9207      */
 9208     public static int codePointCount(CharSequence seq, int beginIndex, int endIndex) {
 9209         int length = seq.length();
 9210         if (beginIndex < 0 || endIndex > length || beginIndex > endIndex) {
 9211             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9212         }
 9213         int n = endIndex - beginIndex;
 9214         for (int i = beginIndex; i < endIndex; ) {
 9215             if (isHighSurrogate(seq.charAt(i++)) && i < endIndex &&
 9216                 isLowSurrogate(seq.charAt(i))) {
 9217                 n--;
 9218                 i++;
 9219             }
 9220         }
 9221         return n;
 9222     }
 9223 
 9224     /**
 9225      * Returns the number of Unicode code points in a subarray of the
 9226      * {@code char} array argument. The {@code offset}
 9227      * argument is the index of the first {@code char} of the
 9228      * subarray and the {@code count} argument specifies the
 9229      * length of the subarray in {@code char}s. Unpaired
 9230      * surrogates within the subarray count as one code point each.
 9231      *
 9232      * @param a the {@code char} array
 9233      * @param offset the index of the first {@code char} in the
 9234      * given {@code char} array
 9235      * @param count the length of the subarray in {@code char}s
 9236      * @return the number of Unicode code points in the specified subarray
 9237      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 9238      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if {@code offset} or
 9239      * {@code count} is negative, or if {@code offset +
 9240      * count} is larger than the length of the given array.
 9241      * @since  1.5
 9242      */
 9243     public static int codePointCount(char[] a, int offset, int count) {
 9244         if (count > a.length - offset || offset < 0 || count < 0) {
 9245             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9246         }
 9247         return codePointCountImpl(a, offset, count);
 9248     }
 9249 
 9250     static int codePointCountImpl(char[] a, int offset, int count) {
 9251         int endIndex = offset + count;
 9252         int n = count;
 9253         for (int i = offset; i < endIndex; ) {
 9254             if (isHighSurrogate(a[i++]) && i < endIndex &&
 9255                 isLowSurrogate(a[i])) {
 9256                 n--;
 9257                 i++;
 9258             }
 9259         }
 9260         return n;
 9261     }
 9262 
 9263     /**
 9264      * Returns the index within the given char sequence that is offset
 9265      * from the given {@code index} by {@code codePointOffset}
 9266      * code points. Unpaired surrogates within the text range given by
 9267      * {@code index} and {@code codePointOffset} count as
 9268      * one code point each.
 9269      *
 9270      * @param seq the char sequence
 9271      * @param index the index to be offset
 9272      * @param codePointOffset the offset in code points
 9273      * @return the index within the char sequence
 9274      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code seq} is null.
 9275      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if {@code index}
 9276      *   is negative or larger then the length of the char sequence,
 9277      *   or if {@code codePointOffset} is positive and the
 9278      *   subsequence starting with {@code index} has fewer than
 9279      *   {@code codePointOffset} code points, or if
 9280      *   {@code codePointOffset} is negative and the subsequence
 9281      *   before {@code index} has fewer than the absolute value
 9282      *   of {@code codePointOffset} code points.
 9283      * @since 1.5
 9284      */
 9285     public static int offsetByCodePoints(CharSequence seq, int index,
 9286                                          int codePointOffset) {
 9287         int length = seq.length();
 9288         if (index < 0 || index > length) {
 9289             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9290         }
 9291 
 9292         int x = index;
 9293         if (codePointOffset >= 0) {
 9294             int i;
 9295             for (i = 0; x < length && i < codePointOffset; i++) {
 9296                 if (isHighSurrogate(seq.charAt(x++)) && x < length &&
 9297                     isLowSurrogate(seq.charAt(x))) {
 9298                     x++;
 9299                 }
 9300             }
 9301             if (i < codePointOffset) {
 9302                 throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9303             }
 9304         } else {
 9305             int i;
 9306             for (i = codePointOffset; x > 0 && i < 0; i++) {
 9307                 if (isLowSurrogate(seq.charAt(--x)) && x > 0 &&
 9308                     isHighSurrogate(seq.charAt(x-1))) {
 9309                     x--;
 9310                 }
 9311             }
 9312             if (i < 0) {
 9313                 throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9314             }
 9315         }
 9316         return x;
 9317     }
 9318 
 9319     /**
 9320      * Returns the index within the given {@code char} subarray
 9321      * that is offset from the given {@code index} by
 9322      * {@code codePointOffset} code points. The
 9323      * {@code start} and {@code count} arguments specify a
 9324      * subarray of the {@code char} array. Unpaired surrogates
 9325      * within the text range given by {@code index} and
 9326      * {@code codePointOffset} count as one code point each.
 9327      *
 9328      * @param a the {@code char} array
 9329      * @param start the index of the first {@code char} of the
 9330      * subarray
 9331      * @param count the length of the subarray in {@code char}s
 9332      * @param index the index to be offset
 9333      * @param codePointOffset the offset in code points
 9334      * @return the index within the subarray
 9335      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 9336      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException
 9337      *   if {@code start} or {@code count} is negative,
 9338      *   or if {@code start + count} is larger than the length of
 9339      *   the given array,
 9340      *   or if {@code index} is less than {@code start} or
 9341      *   larger then {@code start + count},
 9342      *   or if {@code codePointOffset} is positive and the text range
 9343      *   starting with {@code index} and ending with {@code start + count - 1}
 9344      *   has fewer than {@code codePointOffset} code
 9345      *   points,
 9346      *   or if {@code codePointOffset} is negative and the text range
 9347      *   starting with {@code start} and ending with {@code index - 1}
 9348      *   has fewer than the absolute value of
 9349      *   {@code codePointOffset} code points.
 9350      * @since 1.5
 9351      */
 9352     public static int offsetByCodePoints(char[] a, int start, int count,
 9353                                          int index, int codePointOffset) {
 9354         if (count > a.length-start || start < 0 || count < 0
 9355             || index < start || index > start+count) {
 9356             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9357         }
 9358         return offsetByCodePointsImpl(a, start, count, index, codePointOffset);
 9359     }
 9360 
 9361     static int offsetByCodePointsImpl(char[]a, int start, int count,
 9362                                       int index, int codePointOffset) {
 9363         int x = index;
 9364         if (codePointOffset >= 0) {
 9365             int limit = start + count;
 9366             int i;
 9367             for (i = 0; x < limit && i < codePointOffset; i++) {
 9368                 if (isHighSurrogate(a[x++]) && x < limit &&
 9369                     isLowSurrogate(a[x])) {
 9370                     x++;
 9371                 }
 9372             }
 9373             if (i < codePointOffset) {
 9374                 throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9375             }
 9376         } else {
 9377             int i;
 9378             for (i = codePointOffset; x > start && i < 0; i++) {
 9379                 if (isLowSurrogate(a[--x]) && x > start &&
 9380                     isHighSurrogate(a[x-1])) {
 9381                     x--;
 9382                 }
 9383             }
 9384             if (i < 0) {
 9385                 throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9386             }
 9387         }
 9388         return x;
 9389     }

 9391     /**
 9392      * Determines if the specified character is a lowercase character.
 9393      * <p>
 9394      * A character is lowercase if its general category type, provided
 9395      * by {@code Character.getType(ch)}, is
 9396      * {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}, or it has contributory property
 9397      * Other_Lowercase as defined by the Unicode Standard.
 9398      * <p>
 9399      * The following are examples of lowercase characters:
 9400      * <blockquote><pre>
 9401      * a b c d e f g h i j k l m n o p q r s t u v w x y z
 9402      * '&#92;u00DF' '&#92;u00E0' '&#92;u00E1' '&#92;u00E2' '&#92;u00E3' '&#92;u00E4' '&#92;u00E5' '&#92;u00E6'
 9403      * '&#92;u00E7' '&#92;u00E8' '&#92;u00E9' '&#92;u00EA' '&#92;u00EB' '&#92;u00EC' '&#92;u00ED' '&#92;u00EE'
 9404      * '&#92;u00EF' '&#92;u00F0' '&#92;u00F1' '&#92;u00F2' '&#92;u00F3' '&#92;u00F4' '&#92;u00F5' '&#92;u00F6'
 9405      * '&#92;u00F8' '&#92;u00F9' '&#92;u00FA' '&#92;u00FB' '&#92;u00FC' '&#92;u00FD' '&#92;u00FE' '&#92;u00FF'
 9406      * </pre></blockquote>
 9407      * <p> Many other Unicode characters are lowercase too.
 9408      *
 9409      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9410      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9411      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9412      * the {@link #isLowerCase(int)} method.
 9413      *
 9414      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9415      * @return  {@code true} if the character is lowercase;
 9416      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9417      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
 9418      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(char)
 9419      * @see     Character#toLowerCase(char)
 9420      * @see     Character#getType(char)
 9421      */
 9422     public static boolean isLowerCase(char ch) {
 9423         return isLowerCase((int)ch);
 9424     }
 9425 
 9426     /**
 9427      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a
 9428      * lowercase character.
 9429      * <p>
 9430      * A character is lowercase if its general category type, provided
 9431      * by {@link Character#getType getType(codePoint)}, is
 9432      * {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}, or it has contributory property
 9433      * Other_Lowercase as defined by the Unicode Standard.
 9434      * <p>
 9435      * The following are examples of lowercase characters:
 9436      * <blockquote><pre>
 9437      * a b c d e f g h i j k l m n o p q r s t u v w x y z
 9438      * '&#92;u00DF' '&#92;u00E0' '&#92;u00E1' '&#92;u00E2' '&#92;u00E3' '&#92;u00E4' '&#92;u00E5' '&#92;u00E6'
 9439      * '&#92;u00E7' '&#92;u00E8' '&#92;u00E9' '&#92;u00EA' '&#92;u00EB' '&#92;u00EC' '&#92;u00ED' '&#92;u00EE'
 9440      * '&#92;u00EF' '&#92;u00F0' '&#92;u00F1' '&#92;u00F2' '&#92;u00F3' '&#92;u00F4' '&#92;u00F5' '&#92;u00F6'
 9441      * '&#92;u00F8' '&#92;u00F9' '&#92;u00FA' '&#92;u00FB' '&#92;u00FC' '&#92;u00FD' '&#92;u00FE' '&#92;u00FF'
 9442      * </pre></blockquote>

 9444      *
 9445      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.

 9453      */
 9454     public static boolean isLowerCase(int codePoint) {
 9455         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isLowerCase(codePoint) ||
 9456                CharacterData.of(codePoint).isOtherLowercase(codePoint);
 9457     }

 9505      * '&#92;u00C8' '&#92;u00C9' '&#92;u00CA' '&#92;u00CB' '&#92;u00CC' '&#92;u00CD' '&#92;u00CE' '&#92;u00CF'
 9506      * '&#92;u00D0' '&#92;u00D1' '&#92;u00D2' '&#92;u00D3' '&#92;u00D4' '&#92;u00D5' '&#92;u00D6' '&#92;u00D8'
 9507      * '&#92;u00D9' '&#92;u00DA' '&#92;u00DB' '&#92;u00DC' '&#92;u00DD' '&#92;u00DE'
