 9525     /**
 9526      * Determines if the specified character is a titlecase character.
 9527      * <p>
 9528      * A character is a titlecase character if its general
 9529      * category type, provided by {@code Character.getType(ch)},
 9530      * is {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}.
 9531      * <p>
 9532      * Some characters look like pairs of Latin letters. For example, there
 9533      * is an uppercase letter that looks like "LJ" and has a corresponding
 9534      * lowercase letter that looks like "lj". A third form, which looks like "Lj",
 9535      * is the appropriate form to use when rendering a word in lowercase
 9536      * with initial capitals, as for a book title.
 9537      * <p>
 9538      * These are some of the Unicode characters for which this method returns
 9539      * {@code true}:
 9540      * <ul>
 9541      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER D WITH SMALL LETTER Z WITH CARON}
 9542      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER L WITH SMALL LETTER J}
 9543      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER N WITH SMALL LETTER J}
 9544      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER D WITH SMALL LETTER Z}
 9545      * </ul>
 9546      * <p> Many other Unicode characters are titlecase too.
 9547      *
 9548      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9549      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9550      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9551      * the {@link #isTitleCase(int)} method.
 9552      *
 9553      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9554      * @return  {@code true} if the character is titlecase;
 9555      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9556      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
 9557      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(char)
 9558      * @see     Character#toTitleCase(char)
 9559      * @see     Character#getType(char)
 9560      * @since   1.0.2
 9561      */
 9562     public static boolean isTitleCase(char ch) {
 9563         return isTitleCase((int)ch);
 9564     }
 9565 
 9566     /**
 9567      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a titlecase character.
 9568      * <p>
 9569      * A character is a titlecase character if its general
 9570      * category type, provided by {@link Character#getType(int) getType(codePoint)},
 9571      * is {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}.
 9572      * <p>
 9573      * Some characters look like pairs of Latin letters. For example, there
 9574      * is an uppercase letter that looks like "LJ" and has a corresponding
 9575      * lowercase letter that looks like "lj". A third form, which looks like "Lj",
 9576      * is the appropriate form to use when rendering a word in lowercase
 9577      * with initial capitals, as for a book title.
 9578      * <p>
 9579      * These are some of the Unicode characters for which this method returns
 9580      * {@code true}:
 9581      * <ul>
 9582      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER D WITH SMALL LETTER Z WITH CARON}
 9583      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER L WITH SMALL LETTER J}
 9584      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER N WITH SMALL LETTER J}
 9585      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER D WITH SMALL LETTER Z}
 9586      * </ul>
 9587      * <p> Many other Unicode characters are titlecase too.
 9588      *
 9589      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9590      * @return  {@code true} if the character is titlecase;
 9591      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9592      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(int)
 9593      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(int)
 9594      * @see     Character#toTitleCase(int)
 9595      * @see     Character#getType(int)
 9596      * @since   1.5
 9597      */
 9598     public static boolean isTitleCase(int codePoint) {
 9599         return getType(codePoint) == Character.TITLECASE_LETTER;
 9600     }
 9601 
 9602     /**
 9603      * Determines if the specified character is a digit.
 9604      * <p>
 9605      * A character is a digit if its general category type, provided
 9606      * by {@code Character.getType(ch)}, is
 9607      * {@code DECIMAL_DIGIT_NUMBER}.
 9608      * <p>
 9609      * Some Unicode character ranges that contain digits:
 9610      * <ul>
 9611      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0030'} through {@code '\u005Cu0039'},
 9612      *     ISO-LATIN-1 digits ({@code '0'} through {@code '9'})
 9613      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0660'} through {@code '\u005Cu0669'},
 9614      *     Arabic-Indic digits
 9615      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu06F0'} through {@code '\u005Cu06F9'},
 9616      *     Extended Arabic-Indic digits
 9617      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0966'} through {@code '\u005Cu096F'},
 9618      *     Devanagari digits
 9619      * <li>{@code '\u005CuFF10'} through {@code '\u005CuFF19'},
 9620      *     Fullwidth digits
 9621      * </ul>
 9622      *
 9623      * Many other character ranges contain digits as well.
 9624      *
 9625      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9626      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9627      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9628      * the {@link #isDigit(int)} method.
 9629      *
 9630      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9631      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a digit;
 9632      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9633      * @see     Character#digit(char, int)
 9634      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
 9635      * @see     Character#getType(char)
 9636      */
 9637     public static boolean isDigit(char ch) {
 9638         return isDigit((int)ch);
 9639     }
 9640 
 9641     /**
 9642      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a digit.
 9643      * <p>
 9644      * A character is a digit if its general category type, provided
 9645      * by {@link Character#getType(int) getType(codePoint)}, is
 9646      * {@code DECIMAL_DIGIT_NUMBER}.
 9647      * <p>
 9648      * Some Unicode character ranges that contain digits:
 9649      * <ul>
 9650      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0030'} through {@code '\u005Cu0039'},
 9651      *     ISO-LATIN-1 digits ({@code '0'} through {@code '9'})
 9652      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0660'} through {@code '\u005Cu0669'},
 9653      *     Arabic-Indic digits
 9654      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu06F0'} through {@code '\u005Cu06F9'},
 9655      *     Extended Arabic-Indic digits
 9656      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0966'} through {@code '\u005Cu096F'},
 9657      *     Devanagari digits
 9658      * <li>{@code '\u005CuFF10'} through {@code '\u005CuFF19'},
 9659      *     Fullwidth digits
 9660      * </ul>
 9661      *
 9662      * Many other character ranges contain digits as well.
 9663      *
 9664      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9665      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a digit;
 9666      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9667      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
 9668      * @see     Character#getType(int)
 9669      * @since   1.5
 9670      */
 9671     public static boolean isDigit(int codePoint) {
 9672         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isDigit(codePoint);
 9673     }
 9674 
 9675     /**
 9676      * Determines if a character is defined in Unicode.
 9677      * <p>
 9678      * A character is defined if at least one of the following is true:
 9679      * <ul>
 9680      * <li>It has an entry in the UnicodeData file.
 9681      * <li>It has a value in a range defined by the UnicodeData file.
 9682      * </ul>
 9683      *
 9684      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9685      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9686      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9687      * the {@link #isDefined(int)} method.
 9688      *
 9689      * @param   ch   the character to be tested
 9690      * @return  {@code true} if the character has a defined meaning
 9691      *          in Unicode; {@code false} otherwise.
 9692      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
 9693      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
 9694      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
 9695      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
 9696      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(char)
 9697      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(char)
 9698      * @since   1.0.2
 9699      */
 9700     public static boolean isDefined(char ch) {
 9701         return isDefined((int)ch);
 9702     }
 9703 
 9704     /**
 9705      * Determines if a character (Unicode code point) is defined in Unicode.
 9706      * <p>
 9707      * A character is defined if at least one of the following is true:
 9708      * <ul>
 9709      * <li>It has an entry in the UnicodeData file.
 9710      * <li>It has a value in a range defined by the UnicodeData file.
 9711      * </ul>
 9712      *
 9713      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9714      * @return  {@code true} if the character has a defined meaning
 9715      *          in Unicode; {@code false} otherwise.
 9716      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
 9717      * @see     Character#isLetter(int)
 9718      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(int)
 9719      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(int)
 9720      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(int)
 9721      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(int)
 9722      * @since   1.5
 9723      */
 9724     public static boolean isDefined(int codePoint) {
 9725         return getType(codePoint) != Character.UNASSIGNED;
 9726     }
 9727 
 9728     /**
 9729      * Determines if the specified character is a letter.
 9730      * <p>
 9731      * A character is considered to be a letter if its general
 9732      * category type, provided by {@code Character.getType(ch)},
 9733      * is any of the following:
 9734      * <ul>
 9735      * <li> {@code UPPERCASE_LETTER}
 9736      * <li> {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}
 9737      * <li> {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}
 9738      * <li> {@code MODIFIER_LETTER}
 9739      * <li> {@code OTHER_LETTER}
 9740      * </ul>
 9741      *
 9742      * Not all letters have case. Many characters are
 9743      * letters but are neither uppercase nor lowercase nor titlecase.
 9744      *
 9745      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9746      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9747      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9748      * the {@link #isLetter(int)} method.
 9749      *
 9750      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9751      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a letter;
 9752      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9753      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
 9754      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(char)
 9755      * @see     Character#isJavaLetter(char)
 9756      * @see     Character#isJavaLetterOrDigit(char)
 9757      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
 9758      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
 9759      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(char)
 9760      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierStart(char)
 9761      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(char)
 9762      */
 9763     public static boolean isLetter(char ch) {
 9764         return isLetter((int)ch);
 9765     }
 9766 
 9767     /**
 9768      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a letter.
 9769      * <p>
 9770      * A character is considered to be a letter if its general
 9771      * category type, provided by {@link Character#getType(int) getType(codePoint)},
 9772      * is any of the following:
 9773      * <ul>
 9774      * <li> {@code UPPERCASE_LETTER}
 9775      * <li> {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}
 9776      * <li> {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}
 9777      * <li> {@code MODIFIER_LETTER}
 9778      * <li> {@code OTHER_LETTER}
 9779      * </ul>
 9780      *
 9781      * Not all letters have case. Many characters are
 9782      * letters but are neither uppercase nor lowercase nor titlecase.
 9783      *
 9784      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9785      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a letter;
 9786      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9787      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
 9788      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(int)
 9789      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(int)
 9790      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(int)
 9791      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(int)
 9792      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierStart(int)
 9793      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(int)
 9794      * @since   1.5
 9795      */
 9796     public static boolean isLetter(int codePoint) {
 9797         return ((((1 << Character.UPPERCASE_LETTER) |
 9798             (1 << Character.LOWERCASE_LETTER) |
 9799             (1 << Character.TITLECASE_LETTER) |
 9800             (1 << Character.MODIFIER_LETTER) |
 9801             (1 << Character.OTHER_LETTER)) >> getType(codePoint)) & 1)
 9802             != 0;
 9803     }
 9804 
 9805     /**
 9806      * Determines if the specified character is a letter or digit.
 9807      * <p>
 9808      * A character is considered to be a letter or digit if either
 9809      * {@code Character.isLetter(char ch)} or
 9810      * {@code Character.isDigit(char ch)} returns
 9811      * {@code true} for the character.
 9812      *
 9813      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9814      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9815      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9816      * the {@link #isLetterOrDigit(int)} method.
 9817      *
 9818      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9819      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a letter or digit;
 9820      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9821      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
 9822      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(char)
 9823      * @see     Character#isJavaLetter(char)
 9824      * @see     Character#isJavaLetterOrDigit(char)
 9825      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
 9826      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(char)
 9827      * @since   1.0.2
 9828      */
 9829     public static boolean isLetterOrDigit(char ch) {
 9830         return isLetterOrDigit((int)ch);
 9831     }
 9832 
 9833     /**
 9834      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a letter or digit.
 9835      * <p>
 9836      * A character is considered to be a letter or digit if either
 9837      * {@link #isLetter(int) isLetter(codePoint)} or
 9838      * {@link #isDigit(int) isDigit(codePoint)} returns
 9839      * {@code true} for the character.
 9840      *
 9841      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9842      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a letter or digit;
 9843      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9844      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
 9845      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(int)
 9846      * @see     Character#isLetter(int)
 9847      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(int)
 9848      * @since   1.5
 9849      */
 9850     public static boolean isLetterOrDigit(int codePoint) {
 9851         return ((((1 << Character.UPPERCASE_LETTER) |
 9852             (1 << Character.LOWERCASE_LETTER) |
 9853             (1 << Character.TITLECASE_LETTER) |
 9854             (1 << Character.MODIFIER_LETTER) |
 9855             (1 << Character.OTHER_LETTER) |
 9856             (1 << Character.DECIMAL_DIGIT_NUMBER)) >> getType(codePoint)) & 1)
 9857             != 0;
 9858     }

 9860     /**
 9861      * Determines if the specified character is permissible as the first
 9862      * character in a Java identifier.
 9863      * <p>
 9864      * A character may start a Java identifier if and only if
 9865      * one of the following conditions is true:
 9866      * <ul>
 9867      * <li> {@link #isLetter(char) isLetter(ch)} returns {@code true}
 9868      * <li> {@link #getType(char) getType(ch)} returns {@code LETTER_NUMBER}
 9869      * <li> {@code ch} is a currency symbol (such as {@code '$'})
 9870      * <li> {@code ch} is a connecting punctuation character (such as {@code '_'}).
 9871      * </ul>
 9872      *
 9873      * @param   ch the character to be tested.
 9874      * @return  {@code true} if the character may start a Java
 9875      *          identifier; {@code false} otherwise.
 9876      * @see     Character#isJavaLetterOrDigit(char)
 9877      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(char)
 9878      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(char)
 9879      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
 9880      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
 9881      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierStart(char)
 9882      * @since   1.0.2
 9883      * @deprecated Replaced by isJavaIdentifierStart(char).
 9884      */
 9885     @Deprecated(since="1.1")
 9886     public static boolean isJavaLetter(char ch) {
 9887         return isJavaIdentifierStart(ch);
 9888     }

 9890     /**
 9891      * Determines if the specified character may be part of a Java
 9892      * identifier as other than the first character.
 9893      * <p>
 9894      * A character may be part of a Java identifier if and only if one
 9895      * of the following conditions is true:
 9896      * <ul>
 9897      * <li>  it is a letter
 9898      * <li>  it is a currency symbol (such as {@code '$'})
 9899      * <li>  it is a connecting punctuation character (such as {@code '_'})
 9900      * <li>  it is a digit
 9901      * <li>  it is a numeric letter (such as a Roman numeral character)
 9902      * <li>  it is a combining mark
 9903      * <li>  it is a non-spacing mark
 9904      * <li> {@code isIdentifierIgnorable} returns
 9905      * {@code true} for the character.
 9906      * </ul>
 9907      *
 9908      * @param   ch the character to be tested.
 9909      * @return  {@code true} if the character may be part of a
 9910      *          Java identifier; {@code false} otherwise.
 9911      * @see     Character#isJavaLetter(char)
 9912      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(char)
 9913      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(char)
 9914      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
 9915      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
 9916      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(char)
 9917      * @see     Character#isIdentifierIgnorable(char)
 9918      * @since   1.0.2
 9919      * @deprecated Replaced by isJavaIdentifierPart(char).
 9920      */
 9921     @Deprecated(since="1.1")
 9922     public static boolean isJavaLetterOrDigit(char ch) {
 9923         return isJavaIdentifierPart(ch);
 9924     }

 9926     /**
 9927      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is alphabetic.
 9928      * <p>
 9929      * A character is considered to be alphabetic if its general category type,
 9930      * provided by {@link Character#getType(int) getType(codePoint)}, is any of
 9931      * the following:
 9932      * <ul>
 9933      * <li> {@code UPPERCASE_LETTER}
 9934      * <li> {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}
 9935      * <li> {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}
 9936      * <li> {@code MODIFIER_LETTER}
 9937      * <li> {@code OTHER_LETTER}
 9938      * <li> {@code LETTER_NUMBER}
 9939      * </ul>
 9940      * or it has contributory property Other_Alphabetic as defined by the
 9941      * Unicode Standard.
 9942      *
 9943      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9944      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a Unicode alphabet
 9945      *          character, {@code false} otherwise.
 9946      * @since   1.7
 9947      */
 9948     public static boolean isAlphabetic(int codePoint) {
 9949         return (((((1 << Character.UPPERCASE_LETTER) |
 9950             (1 << Character.LOWERCASE_LETTER) |
 9951             (1 << Character.TITLECASE_LETTER) |
 9952             (1 << Character.MODIFIER_LETTER) |
 9953             (1 << Character.OTHER_LETTER) |
 9954             (1 << Character.LETTER_NUMBER)) >> getType(codePoint)) & 1) != 0) ||
 9955             CharacterData.of(codePoint).isOtherAlphabetic(codePoint);
 9956     }

 9968     public static boolean isIdeographic(int codePoint) {
 9969         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isIdeographic(codePoint);
 9970     }

10074      * conditions are true:
10075      * <ul>
10076      * <li>  it is a letter
10077      * <li>  it is a currency symbol (such as {@code '$'})
10078      * <li>  it is a connecting punctuation character (such as {@code '_'})
10079      * <li>  it is a digit
10080      * <li>  it is a numeric letter (such as a Roman numeral character)
10081      * <li>  it is a combining mark
10082      * <li>  it is a non-spacing mark
10083      * <li> {@link #isIdentifierIgnorable(int)
10084      * isIdentifierIgnorable(codePoint)} returns {@code true} for

10086      * </ul>
10087      *

10089      * @return {@code true} if the character may be part of a
10090      *          Java identifier; {@code false} otherwise.
10091      * @see     Character#isIdentifierIgnorable(int)
10092      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(int)
10093      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(int)

10102     /**
10103      * Determines if the specified character is permissible as the
10104      * first character in a Unicode identifier.
10105      * <p>
10106      * A character may start a Unicode identifier if and only if
10107      * one of the following conditions is true:
10108      * <ul>
10109      * <li> {@link #isLetter(char) isLetter(ch)} returns {@code true}
10110      * <li> {@link #getType(char) getType(ch)} returns
10111      *      {@code LETTER_NUMBER}.
10112      * <li> it is an <a href="http://www.unicode.org/reports/tr44/#Other_ID_Start">
10113      *      {@code Other_ID_Start}</a> character.
10114      * </ul>
10115      * <p>
10116      * This method conforms to <a href="https://unicode.org/reports/tr31/#R1">
10117      * UAX31-R1: Default Identifiers</a> requirement of the Unicode Standard,
10118      * with the following profile of UAX31:
10119      * <pre>
10120      * Start := ID_Start + 'VERTICAL TILDE' (U+2E2F)
10121      * </pre>
10122      * {@code 'VERTICAL TILDE'} is added to {@code Start} for backward
10123      * compatibility.
10124      *
10125      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10126      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10127      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10128      * the {@link #isUnicodeIdentifierStart(int)} method.
10129      *
10130      * @param   ch      the character to be tested.
10131      * @return  {@code true} if the character may start a Unicode
10132      *          identifier; {@code false} otherwise.
10133      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(char)
10134      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
10135      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(char)
10136      * @since   1.1
10137      */
10138     public static boolean isUnicodeIdentifierStart(char ch) {
10139         return isUnicodeIdentifierStart((int)ch);
10140     }

10142     /**
10143      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is permissible as the
10144      * first character in a Unicode identifier.
10145      * <p>
10146      * A character may start a Unicode identifier if and only if
10147      * one of the following conditions is true:
10148      * <ul>
10149      * <li> {@link #isLetter(int) isLetter(codePoint)}
10150      *      returns {@code true}
10151      * <li> {@link #getType(int) getType(codePoint)}
10152      *      returns {@code LETTER_NUMBER}.
10153      * <li> it is an <a href="http://www.unicode.org/reports/tr44/#Other_ID_Start">
10154      *      {@code Other_ID_Start}</a> character.
10155      * </ul>
10156      * <p>
10157      * This method conforms to <a href="https://unicode.org/reports/tr31/#R1">
10158      * UAX31-R1: Default Identifiers</a> requirement of the Unicode Standard,
10159      * with the following profile of UAX31:
10160      * <pre>
10161      * Start := ID_Start + 'VERTICAL TILDE' (U+2E2F)
10162      * </pre>
10163      * {@code 'VERTICAL TILDE'} is added to {@code Start} for backward
10164      * compatibility.
10165      *
10166      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
10167      * @return  {@code true} if the character may start a Unicode
10168      *          identifier; {@code false} otherwise.
10169      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(int)
10170      * @see     Character#isLetter(int)
10171      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(int)
10172      * @since   1.5
10173      */
10174     public static boolean isUnicodeIdentifierStart(int codePoint) {
10175         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isUnicodeIdentifierStart(codePoint);
10176     }

10178     /**
10179      * Determines if the specified character may be part of a Unicode
10180      * identifier as other than the first character.
10181      * <p>
10182      * A character may be part of a Unicode identifier if and only if
10183      * one of the following statements is true:
10184      * <ul>
10185      * <li>  it is a letter
10186      * <li>  it is a connecting punctuation character (such as {@code '_'})
10187      * <li>  it is a digit
10188      * <li>  it is a numeric letter (such as a Roman numeral character)
10189      * <li>  it is a combining mark
10190      * <li>  it is a non-spacing mark
10191      * <li> {@code isIdentifierIgnorable} returns
10192      * {@code true} for this character.
10193      * <li> it is an <a href="http://www.unicode.org/reports/tr44/#Other_ID_Start">
10194      *      {@code Other_ID_Start}</a> character.
10195      * <li> it is an <a href="http://www.unicode.org/reports/tr44/#Other_ID_Continue">
10196      *      {@code Other_ID_Continue}</a> character.
10197      * </ul>
10198      * <p>
10199      * This method conforms to <a href="https://unicode.org/reports/tr31/#R1">
10200      * UAX31-R1: Default Identifiers</a> requirement of the Unicode Standard,
10201      * with the following profile of UAX31:
10202      * <pre>
10203      * Continue := Start + ID_Continue + ignorable
10204      * Medial := empty
10205      * ignorable := isIdentifierIgnorable(char) returns true for the character
10206      * </pre>
10207      * {@code ignorable} is added to {@code Continue} for backward
10208      * compatibility.
10209      *
10210      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10211      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10212      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10213      * the {@link #isUnicodeIdentifierPart(int)} method.
10214      *
10215      * @param   ch      the character to be tested.
10216      * @return  {@code true} if the character may be part of a
10217      *          Unicode identifier; {@code false} otherwise.
10218      * @see     Character#isIdentifierIgnorable(char)
10219      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(char)
10220      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
10221      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierStart(char)
10222      * @since   1.1
10223      */
10224     public static boolean isUnicodeIdentifierPart(char ch) {
10225         return isUnicodeIdentifierPart((int)ch);
10226     }

10338     /**
10339      * Converts the character argument to lowercase using case
10340      * mapping information from the UnicodeData file.
10341      * <p>
10342      * Note that
10343      * {@code Character.isLowerCase(Character.toLowerCase(ch))}
10344      * does not always return {@code true} for some ranges of
10345      * characters, particularly those that are symbols or ideographs.
10346      *
10347      * <p>In general, {@link String#toLowerCase()} should be used to map
10348      * characters to lowercase. {@code String} case mapping methods
10349      * have several benefits over {@code Character} case mapping methods.
10350      * {@code String} case mapping methods can perform locale-sensitive
10351      * mappings, context-sensitive mappings, and 1:M character mappings, whereas
10352      * the {@code Character} case mapping methods cannot.
10353      *
10354      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10355      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10356      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10357      * the {@link #toLowerCase(int)} method.
10358      *
10359      * @param   ch   the character to be converted.
10360      * @return  the lowercase equivalent of the character, if any;
10361      *          otherwise, the character itself.
10362      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
10363      * @see     String#toLowerCase()
10364      */
10365     public static char toLowerCase(char ch) {
10366         return (char)toLowerCase((int)ch);
10367     }

10517     /**
10518      * Returns the numeric value of the character {@code ch} in the
10519      * specified radix.
10520      * <p>
10521      * If the radix is not in the range {@code MIN_RADIX} &le;
10522      * {@code radix} &le; {@code MAX_RADIX} or if the
10523      * value of {@code ch} is not a valid digit in the specified
10524      * radix, {@code -1} is returned. A character is a valid digit
10525      * if at least one of the following is true:
10526      * <ul>
10527      * <li>The method {@code isDigit} is {@code true} of the character
10528      *     and the Unicode decimal digit value of the character (or its
10529      *     single-character decomposition) is less than the specified radix.
10530      *     In this case the decimal digit value is returned.
10531      * <li>The character is one of the uppercase Latin letters
10532      *     {@code 'A'} through {@code 'Z'} and its code is less than
10533      *     {@code radix + 'A' - 10}.
10534      *     In this case, {@code ch - 'A' + 10}
10535      *     is returned.
10536      * <li>The character is one of the lowercase Latin letters
10537      *     {@code 'a'} through {@code 'z'} and its code is less than
10538      *     {@code radix + 'a' - 10}.
10539      *     In this case, {@code ch - 'a' + 10}
10540      *     is returned.
10541      * <li>The character is one of the fullwidth uppercase Latin letters A
10542      *     ({@code '\u005CuFF21'}) through Z ({@code '\u005CuFF3A'})
10543      *     and its code is less than
10544      *     {@code radix + '\u005CuFF21' - 10}.
10545      *     In this case, {@code ch - '\u005CuFF21' + 10}
10546      *     is returned.
10547      * <li>The character is one of the fullwidth lowercase Latin letters a
10548      *     ({@code '\u005CuFF41'}) through z ({@code '\u005CuFF5A'})
10549      *     and its code is less than
10550      *     {@code radix + '\u005CuFF41' - 10}.
10551      *     In this case, {@code ch - '\u005CuFF41' + 10}
10552      *     is returned.
10553      * </ul>
10554      *
10555      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10556      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10557      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10558      * the {@link #digit(int, int)} method.
10559      *
10560      * @param   ch      the character to be converted.
10561      * @param   radix   the radix.
10562      * @return  the numeric value represented by the character in the
10563      *          specified radix.
10564      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
10565      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
10566      */
10567     public static int digit(char ch, int radix) {
10568         return digit((int)ch, radix);
10569     }
10570 
10571     /**
10572      * Returns the numeric value of the specified character (Unicode
10573      * code point) in the specified radix.
10574      *
10575      * <p>If the radix is not in the range {@code MIN_RADIX} &le;
10576      * {@code radix} &le; {@code MAX_RADIX} or if the
10577      * character is not a valid digit in the specified
10578      * radix, {@code -1} is returned. A character is a valid digit
10579      * if at least one of the following is true:
10580      * <ul>
10581      * <li>The method {@link #isDigit(int) isDigit(codePoint)} is {@code true} of the character
10582      *     and the Unicode decimal digit value of the character (or its
10583      *     single-character decomposition) is less than the specified radix.
10584      *     In this case the decimal digit value is returned.
10585      * <li>The character is one of the uppercase Latin letters
10586      *     {@code 'A'} through {@code 'Z'} and its code is less than
10587      *     {@code radix + 'A' - 10}.
10588      *     In this case, {@code codePoint - 'A' + 10}
10589      *     is returned.
10590      * <li>The character is one of the lowercase Latin letters
10591      *     {@code 'a'} through {@code 'z'} and its code is less than
10592      *     {@code radix + 'a' - 10}.
10593      *     In this case, {@code codePoint - 'a' + 10}
10594      *     is returned.
10595      * <li>The character is one of the fullwidth uppercase Latin letters A
10596      *     ({@code '\u005CuFF21'}) through Z ({@code '\u005CuFF3A'})
10597      *     and its code is less than
10598      *     {@code radix + '\u005CuFF21' - 10}.
10599      *     In this case,
10600      *     {@code codePoint - '\u005CuFF21' + 10}
10601      *     is returned.
10602      * <li>The character is one of the fullwidth lowercase Latin letters a
10603      *     ({@code '\u005CuFF41'}) through z ({@code '\u005CuFF5A'})
10604      *     and its code is less than
10605      *     {@code radix + '\u005CuFF41'- 10}.
10606      *     In this case,
10607      *     {@code codePoint - '\u005CuFF41' + 10}
10608      *     is returned.
10609      * </ul>
10610      *
10611      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
10612      * @param   radix   the radix.
10613      * @return  the numeric value represented by the character in the
10614      *          specified radix.
10615      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
10616      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
10617      * @since   1.5
10618      */
10619     public static int digit(int codePoint, int radix) {
10620         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).digit(codePoint, radix);
10621     }

10623     /**
10624      * Returns the {@code int} value that the specified Unicode
10625      * character represents. For example, the character
10626      * {@code '\u005Cu216C'} (the roman numeral fifty) will return
10627      * an int with a value of 50.
10628      * <p>
10629      * The letters A-Z in their uppercase ({@code '\u005Cu0041'} through
10630      * {@code '\u005Cu005A'}), lowercase
10631      * ({@code '\u005Cu0061'} through {@code '\u005Cu007A'}), and
10632      * full width variant ({@code '\u005CuFF21'} through
10633      * {@code '\u005CuFF3A'} and {@code '\u005CuFF41'} through
10634      * {@code '\u005CuFF5A'}) forms have numeric values from 10
10635      * through 35. This is independent of the Unicode specification,
10636      * which does not assign numeric values to these {@code char}
10637      * values.
10638      * <p>
10639      * If the character does not have a numeric value, then -1 is returned.
10640      * If the character has a numeric value that cannot be represented as a
10641      * nonnegative integer (for example, a fractional value), then -2
10642      * is returned.
10643      *
10644      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10645      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10646      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10647      * the {@link #getNumericValue(int)} method.
10648      *
10649      * @param   ch      the character to be converted.
10650      * @return  the numeric value of the character, as a nonnegative {@code int}
10651      *          value; -2 if the character has a numeric value but the value
10652      *          can not be represented as a nonnegative {@code int} value;
10653      *          -1 if the character has no numeric value.
10654      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
10655      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
10656      * @since   1.1
10657      */
10658     public static int getNumericValue(char ch) {
10659         return getNumericValue((int)ch);
10660     }
10661 
10662     /**
10663      * Returns the {@code int} value that the specified
10664      * character (Unicode code point) represents. For example, the character
10665      * {@code '\u005Cu216C'} (the Roman numeral fifty) will return
10666      * an {@code int} with a value of 50.
10667      * <p>
10668      * The letters A-Z in their uppercase ({@code '\u005Cu0041'} through
10669      * {@code '\u005Cu005A'}), lowercase
10670      * ({@code '\u005Cu0061'} through {@code '\u005Cu007A'}), and
10671      * full width variant ({@code '\u005CuFF21'} through
10672      * {@code '\u005CuFF3A'} and {@code '\u005CuFF41'} through
10673      * {@code '\u005CuFF5A'}) forms have numeric values from 10
10674      * through 35. This is independent of the Unicode specification,
10675      * which does not assign numeric values to these {@code char}
10676      * values.
10677      * <p>
10678      * If the character does not have a numeric value, then -1 is returned.
10679      * If the character has a numeric value that cannot be represented as a
10680      * nonnegative integer (for example, a fractional value), then -2
10681      * is returned.
10682      *
10683      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
10684      * @return  the numeric value of the character, as a nonnegative {@code int}
10685      *          value; -2 if the character has a numeric value but the value
10686      *          can not be represented as a nonnegative {@code int} value;
10687      *          -1 if the character has no numeric value.
10688      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
10689      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
10690      * @since   1.5
10691      */
10692     public static int getNumericValue(int codePoint) {
10693         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).getNumericValue(codePoint);
10694     }
10695 
10696     /**
10697      * Determines if the specified character is ISO-LATIN-1 white space.
10698      * This method returns {@code true} for the following five
10699      * characters only:
10700      * <table class="striped">
10701      * <caption style="display:none">truechars</caption>
10702      * <thead>
10703      * <tr><th scope="col">Character
10704      *     <th scope="col">Code
10705      *     <th scope="col">Name
10706      * </thead>
10707      * <tbody>
10708      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code '\t'}</th>            <td>{@code U+0009}</td>
10709      *     <td>{@code HORIZONTAL TABULATION}</td></tr>
10710      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code '\n'}</th>            <td>{@code U+000A}</td>
10711      *     <td>{@code NEW LINE}</td></tr>
10712      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code '\f'}</th>            <td>{@code U+000C}</td>
10713      *     <td>{@code FORM FEED}</td></tr>
10714      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code '\r'}</th>            <td>{@code U+000D}</td>
10715      *     <td>{@code CARRIAGE RETURN}</td></tr>
10716      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code ' '}</th>  <td>{@code U+0020}</td>
10717      *     <td>{@code SPACE}</td></tr>
10718      * </tbody>
10719      * </table>
10720      *
10721      * @param      ch   the character to be tested.
10722      * @return     {@code true} if the character is ISO-LATIN-1 white
10723      *             space; {@code false} otherwise.
10724      * @see        Character#isSpaceChar(char)
10725      * @see        Character#isWhitespace(char)
10726      * @deprecated Replaced by isWhitespace(char).
10727      */
10728     @Deprecated(since="1.1")
10729     public static boolean isSpace(char ch) {
10730         return (ch <= 0x0020) &&
10731             (((((1L << 0x0009) |
10732             (1L << 0x000A) |
10733             (1L << 0x000C) |
10734             (1L << 0x000D) |
10735             (1L << 0x0020)) >> ch) & 1L) != 0);
10736     }
10737 
10738 
10739     /**
10740      * Determines if the specified character is a Unicode space character.
10741      * A character is considered to be a space character if and only if
10742      * it is specified to be a space character by the Unicode Standard. This
10743      * method returns true if the character's general category type is any of
10744      * the following:
10745      * <ul>
10746      * <li> {@code SPACE_SEPARATOR}
10747      * <li> {@code LINE_SEPARATOR}
10748      * <li> {@code PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR}
10749      * </ul>
10750      *
10751      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10752      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10753      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10754      * the {@link #isSpaceChar(int)} method.
10755      *
10756      * @param   ch      the character to be tested.
10757      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a space character;
10758      *          {@code false} otherwise.
10759      * @see     Character#isWhitespace(char)
10760      * @since   1.1
10761      */
10762     public static boolean isSpaceChar(char ch) {
10763         return isSpaceChar((int)ch);
10764     }
10765 
10766     /**
10767      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a
10768      * Unicode space character.  A character is considered to be a
10769      * space character if and only if it is specified to be a space
10770      * character by the Unicode Standard. This method returns true if
10771      * the character's general category type is any of the following:
10772      *
10773      * <ul>
10774      * <li> {@link #SPACE_SEPARATOR}
10775      * <li> {@link #LINE_SEPARATOR}
10776      * <li> {@link #PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR}
10777      * </ul>
10778      *
10779      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
10780      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a space character;
10781      *          {@code false} otherwise.
10782      * @see     Character#isWhitespace(int)
10783      * @since   1.5
10784      */
10785     public static boolean isSpaceChar(int codePoint) {
10786         return ((((1 << Character.SPACE_SEPARATOR) |
10787                   (1 << Character.LINE_SEPARATOR) |
10788                   (1 << Character.PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR)) >> getType(codePoint)) & 1)
10789             != 0;
10790     }
10791 
10792     /**
10793      * Determines if the specified character is white space according to Java.
10794      * A character is a Java whitespace character if and only if it satisfies
10795      * one of the following criteria:
10796      * <ul>
10797      * <li> It is a Unicode space character ({@code SPACE_SEPARATOR},
10798      *      {@code LINE_SEPARATOR}, or {@code PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR})
10799      *      but is not also a non-breaking space ({@code '\u005Cu00A0'},
10800      *      {@code '\u005Cu2007'}, {@code '\u005Cu202F'}).
10801      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Ct'}, U+0009 HORIZONTAL TABULATION.
10802      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cn'}, U+000A LINE FEED.
10803      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu000B'}, U+000B VERTICAL TABULATION.
10804      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cf'}, U+000C FORM FEED.
10805      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cr'}, U+000D CARRIAGE RETURN.
10806      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001C'}, U+001C FILE SEPARATOR.
10807      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001D'}, U+001D GROUP SEPARATOR.
10808      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001E'}, U+001E RECORD SEPARATOR.
10809      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001F'}, U+001F UNIT SEPARATOR.
10810      * </ul>
10811      *
10812      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10813      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10814      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10815      * the {@link #isWhitespace(int)} method.
10816      *
10817      * @param   ch the character to be tested.
10818      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a Java whitespace
10819      *          character; {@code false} otherwise.
10820      * @see     Character#isSpaceChar(char)
10821      * @since   1.1
10822      */
10823     public static boolean isWhitespace(char ch) {
10824         return isWhitespace((int)ch);
10825     }

10827     /**
10828      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is
10829      * white space according to Java.  A character is a Java
10830      * whitespace character if and only if it satisfies one of the
10831      * following criteria:
10832      * <ul>
10833      * <li> It is a Unicode space character ({@link #SPACE_SEPARATOR},
10834      *      {@link #LINE_SEPARATOR}, or {@link #PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR})
10835      *      but is not also a non-breaking space ({@code '\u005Cu00A0'},
10836      *      {@code '\u005Cu2007'}, {@code '\u005Cu202F'}).
10837      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Ct'}, U+0009 HORIZONTAL TABULATION.
10838      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cn'}, U+000A LINE FEED.
10839      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu000B'}, U+000B VERTICAL TABULATION.
10840      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cf'}, U+000C FORM FEED.
10841      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cr'}, U+000D CARRIAGE RETURN.
10842      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001C'}, U+001C FILE SEPARATOR.
10843      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001D'}, U+001D GROUP SEPARATOR.
10844      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001E'}, U+001E RECORD SEPARATOR.
10845      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001F'}, U+001F UNIT SEPARATOR.
10846      * </ul>
10847      *
10848      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
10849      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a Java whitespace
10850      *          character; {@code false} otherwise.
10851      * @see     Character#isSpaceChar(int)
10852      * @since   1.5
10853      */
10854     public static boolean isWhitespace(int codePoint) {
10855         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isWhitespace(codePoint);
10856     }

10858     /**
10859      * Determines if the specified character is an ISO control
10860      * character.  A character is considered to be an ISO control
10861      * character if its code is in the range {@code '\u005Cu0000'}
10862      * through {@code '\u005Cu001F'} or in the range
10863      * {@code '\u005Cu007F'} through {@code '\u005Cu009F'}.
10864      *
10865      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10866      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10867      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10868      * the {@link #isISOControl(int)} method.
10869      *
10870      * @param   ch      the character to be tested.
10871      * @return  {@code true} if the character is an ISO control character;
10872      *          {@code false} otherwise.
10873      *
10874      * @see     Character#isSpaceChar(char)
10875      * @see     Character#isWhitespace(char)
10876      * @since   1.1
10877      */
10878     public static boolean isISOControl(char ch) {
10879         return isISOControl((int)ch);
10880     }
10881 
10882     /**
10883      * Determines if the referenced character (Unicode code point) is an ISO control
10884      * character.  A character is considered to be an ISO control
10885      * character if its code is in the range {@code '\u005Cu0000'}
10886      * through {@code '\u005Cu001F'} or in the range
10887      * {@code '\u005Cu007F'} through {@code '\u005Cu009F'}.
10888      *
10889      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
10890      * @return  {@code true} if the character is an ISO control character;
10891      *          {@code false} otherwise.
10892      * @see     Character#isSpaceChar(int)
10893      * @see     Character#isWhitespace(int)
10894      * @since   1.5
10895      */
10896     public static boolean isISOControl(int codePoint) {
10897         // Optimized form of:
10898         //     (codePoint >= 0x00 && codePoint <= 0x1F) ||
10899         //     (codePoint >= 0x7F && codePoint <= 0x9F);
10900         return codePoint <= 0x9F &&
10901             (codePoint >= 0x7F || (codePoint >>> 5 == 0));
10902     }

10993     /**
10994      * Determines the character representation for a specific digit in
10995      * the specified radix. If the value of {@code radix} is not a
10996      * valid radix, or the value of {@code digit} is not a valid
10997      * digit in the specified radix, the null character
10998      * ({@code '\u005Cu0000'}) is returned.
10999      * <p>
11000      * The {@code radix} argument is valid if it is greater than or
11001      * equal to {@code MIN_RADIX} and less than or equal to
11002      * {@code MAX_RADIX}. The {@code digit} argument is valid if
11003      * {@code 0 <= digit < radix}.
11004      * <p>
11005      * If the digit is less than 10, then
11006      * {@code '0' + digit} is returned. Otherwise, the value
11007      * {@code 'a' + digit - 10} is returned.
11008      *
11009      * @param   digit   the number to convert to a character.
11010      * @param   radix   the radix.
11011      * @return  the {@code char} representation of the specified digit
11012      *          in the specified radix.
11013      * @see     Character#MIN_RADIX
11014      * @see     Character#MAX_RADIX
11015      * @see     Character#digit(char, int)
11016      */
11017     public static char forDigit(int digit, int radix) {
11018         if ((digit >= radix) || (digit < 0)) {
11019             return '\0';
11020         }
11021         if ((radix < Character.MIN_RADIX) || (radix > Character.MAX_RADIX)) {
11022             return '\0';
11023         }
11024         if (digit < 10) {
11025             return (char)('0' + digit);
11026         }
11027         return (char)('a' - 10 + digit);
11028     }
11029 
11030     /**
11031      * Returns the Unicode directionality property for the given
11032      * character.  Character directionality is used to calculate the
11033      * visual ordering of text. The directionality value of undefined
11034      * {@code char} values is {@code DIRECTIONALITY_UNDEFINED}.
11035      *
11036      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
11037      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
11038      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
11039      * the {@link #getDirectionality(int)} method.
11040      *
11041      * @param  ch {@code char} for which the directionality property
11042      *            is requested.
11043      * @return the directionality property of the {@code char} value.
11044      *
11045      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_UNDEFINED
11046      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_LEFT_TO_RIGHT
11047      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_RIGHT_TO_LEFT

11049      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_EUROPEAN_NUMBER

11071     public static byte getDirectionality(char ch) {

11116     /**
11117      * Determines whether the character is mirrored according to the
11118      * Unicode specification.  Mirrored characters should have their
11119      * glyphs horizontally mirrored when displayed in text that is
11120      * right-to-left.  For example, {@code '\u005Cu0028'} LEFT
11121      * PARENTHESIS is semantically defined to be an <i>opening
11122      * parenthesis</i>.  This will appear as a "(" in text that is
11123      * left-to-right but as a ")" in text that is right-to-left.
11124      *
11125      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
11126      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
11127      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
11128      * the {@link #isMirrored(int)} method.
11129      *
11130      * @param  ch {@code char} for which the mirrored property is requested
11131      * @return {@code true} if the char is mirrored, {@code false}
11132      *         if the {@code char} is not mirrored or is not defined.
11133      * @since 1.4
11134      */
11135     public static boolean isMirrored(char ch) {
11136         return isMirrored((int)ch);
11137     }
11138 
11139     /**
11140      * Determines whether the specified character (Unicode code point)
11141      * is mirrored according to the Unicode specification.  Mirrored
11142      * characters should have their glyphs horizontally mirrored when
11143      * displayed in text that is right-to-left.  For example,
11144      * {@code '\u005Cu0028'} LEFT PARENTHESIS is semantically
11145      * defined to be an <i>opening parenthesis</i>.  This will appear
11146      * as a "(" in text that is left-to-right but as a ")" in text
11147      * that is right-to-left.
11148      *
11149      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
11150      * @return  {@code true} if the character is mirrored, {@code false}
11151      *          if the character is not mirrored or is not defined.
11152      * @since   1.5
11153      */
11154     public static boolean isMirrored(int codePoint) {
11155         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isMirrored(codePoint);
11156     }
11157 
11158     /**
11159      * Compares two {@code Character} objects numerically.
11160      *
11161      * @param   anotherCharacter   the {@code Character} to be compared.
11162      * @return  the value {@code 0} if the argument {@code Character}
11163      *          is equal to this {@code Character}; a value less than
11164      *          {@code 0} if this {@code Character} is numerically less
11165      *          than the {@code Character} argument; and a value greater than
11166      *          {@code 0} if this {@code Character} is numerically greater
11167      *          than the {@code Character} argument (unsigned comparison).
11168      *          Note that this is strictly a numerical comparison; it is not
11169      *          locale-dependent.
11170      * @since   1.2
11171      */
11172     public int compareTo(Character anotherCharacter) {
11173         return compare(this.value, anotherCharacter.value);
11174     }
11175 
11176     /**
11177      * Compares two {@code char} values numerically.
11178      * The value returned is identical to what would be returned by:
11179      * <pre>
11180      *    Character.valueOf(x).compareTo(Character.valueOf(y))
11181      * </pre>
11182      *
11183      * @param  x the first {@code char} to compare
11184      * @param  y the second {@code char} to compare
11185      * @return the value {@code 0} if {@code x == y};
11186      *         a value less than {@code 0} if {@code x < y}; and
11187      *         a value greater than {@code 0} if {@code x > y}
11188      * @since 1.7
11189      */
11190     public static int compare(char x, char y) {
11191         return x - y;
11192     }
11193 
11194     /**
11195      * Converts the character (Unicode code point) argument to uppercase using
11196      * information from the UnicodeData file.
11197      *
11198      * @param   codePoint   the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
11199      * @return  either the uppercase equivalent of the character, if
11200      *          any, or an error flag ({@code Character.ERROR})
11201      *          that indicates that a 1:M {@code char} mapping exists.
11202      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
11203      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(char)
11204      * @see     Character#toLowerCase(char)
11205      * @see     Character#toTitleCase(char)
11206      * @since 1.4
11207      */
11208     static int toUpperCaseEx(int codePoint) {
11209         assert isValidCodePoint(codePoint);
11210         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).toUpperCaseEx(codePoint);
11211     }
11212 
11213     /**
11214      * Converts the character (Unicode code point) argument to uppercase using case
11215      * mapping information from the SpecialCasing file in the Unicode
11216      * specification. If a character has no explicit uppercase
11217      * mapping, then the {@code char} itself is returned in the
11218      * {@code char[]}.
11219      *
11220      * @param   codePoint   the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
11221      * @return a {@code char[]} with the uppercased character.
11222      * @since 1.4
11223      */
11224     static char[] toUpperCaseCharArray(int codePoint) {
11225         // As of Unicode 6.0, 1:M uppercasings only happen in the BMP.
11226         assert isBmpCodePoint(codePoint);
11227         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).toUpperCaseCharArray(codePoint);
11228     }
11229 
11230     /**
11231      * The number of bits used to represent a {@code char} value in unsigned
11232      * binary form, constant {@code 16}.
11233      *
11234      * @since 1.5
11235      */
11236     public static final int SIZE = 16;
11237 
11238     /**
11239      * The number of bytes used to represent a {@code char} value in unsigned
11240      * binary form.
11241      *
11242      * @since 1.8
11243      */
11244     public static final int BYTES = SIZE / Byte.SIZE;
11245 
11246     /**
11247      * Returns the value obtained by reversing the order of the bytes in the
11248      * specified {@code char} value.
11249      *
11250      * @param ch The {@code char} of which to reverse the byte order.
11251      * @return the value obtained by reversing (or, equivalently, swapping)
11252      *     the bytes in the specified {@code char} value.
11253      * @since 1.5
11254      */
11255     @HotSpotIntrinsicCandidate
11256     public static char reverseBytes(char ch) {
11257         return (char) (((ch & 0xFF00) >> 8) | (ch << 8));
11258     }
11259 
11260     /**
11261      * Returns the Unicode name of the specified character
11262      * {@code codePoint}, or null if the code point is
11263      * {@link #UNASSIGNED unassigned}.
11264      * <p>
11265      * Note: if the specified character is not assigned a name by
11266      * the <i>UnicodeData</i> file (part of the Unicode Character
11267      * Database maintained by the Unicode Consortium), the returned
11268      * name is the same as the result of expression:
11269      *
11270      * <blockquote>{@code
11271      *     Character.UnicodeBlock.of(codePoint).toString().replace('_', ' ')
11272      *     + " "
11273      *     + Integer.toHexString(codePoint).toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11274      *
11275      * }</blockquote>
11276      *
11277      * @param  codePoint the character (Unicode code point)
11278      *
11279      * @return the Unicode name of the specified character, or null if
11280      *         the code point is unassigned.
11281      *
11282      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified
11283      *            {@code codePoint} is not a valid Unicode
11284      *            code point.
11285      *
11286      * @since 1.7
11287      */
11288     public static String getName(int codePoint) {
11289         if (!isValidCodePoint(codePoint)) {
11290             throw new IllegalArgumentException(
11291                 String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
11292         }
11293         String name = CharacterName.getInstance().getName(codePoint);
11294         if (name != null)
11295             return name;
11296         if (getType(codePoint) == UNASSIGNED)
11297             return null;
11298         UnicodeBlock block = UnicodeBlock.of(codePoint);
11299         if (block != null)
11300             return block.toString().replace('_', ' ') + " "
11301                    + Integer.toHexString(codePoint).toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11302         // should never come here
11303         return Integer.toHexString(codePoint).toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11304     }
11305 
11306     /**
11307      * Returns the code point value of the Unicode character specified by
11308      * the given Unicode character name.
11309      * <p>
11310      * Note: if a character is not assigned a name by the <i>UnicodeData</i>
11311      * file (part of the Unicode Character Database maintained by the Unicode
11312      * Consortium), its name is defined as the result of expression:
11313      *
11314      * <blockquote>{@code
11315      *     Character.UnicodeBlock.of(codePoint).toString().replace('_', ' ')
11316      *     + " "
11317      *     + Integer.toHexString(codePoint).toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11318      *
11319      * }</blockquote>
11320      * <p>
11321      * The {@code name} matching is case insensitive, with any leading and
11322      * trailing whitespace character removed.
11323      *
11324      * @param  name the Unicode character name
11325      *
11326      * @return the code point value of the character specified by its name.
11327      *
11328      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified {@code name}
11329      *         is not a valid Unicode character name.
11330      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code name} is {@code null}
11331      *
11332      * @since 9
11333      */
11334     public static int codePointOf(String name) {
11335         name = name.trim().toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11336         int cp = CharacterName.getInstance().getCodePoint(name);
11337         if (cp != -1)
11338             return cp;
11339         try {
11340             int off = name.lastIndexOf(' ');
11341             if (off != -1) {
11342                 cp = Integer.parseInt(name, off + 1, name.length(), 16);
11343                 if (isValidCodePoint(cp) && name.equals(getName(cp)))
11344                     return cp;
11345             }
11346         } catch (Exception x) {}
11347         throw new IllegalArgumentException("Unrecognized character name :" + name);
11348     }
11349 }
